(Rome) According to what our reporter knows, Italian Prime Minister Mussolini may accept the Anglo-French proposals for a peaceful resolution of the Italian-Abyssinian dispute in principle and use them as a basis for negotiation. However, it is expected that these negotiations will not only take a very long time but will also be very thorny. It is generally believed that the objections that Italy may raise to the Anglo-French proposals will be limited to the following points: (1) Italy insists that the so-called Abyssinian outlet to the sea must be chosen in the territory of the Italian colony and can only be designated as a free port for Abyssinia to access the sea, and cannot be a territorial concession to Abyssinia. (3) Italy has always wanted to open a corridor between the two Italian colonies of Eritrea and Somaliland so that they can be connected to each other. Therefore, although Italy can give up its claim to occupy the entire Harar province, it is expected that it will still insist on controlling most of the land in the province so that traffic between the Ogaden region and the Danakil region can be unimpeded, thereby realizing Italy's plan to connect the above two colonies. (5) Regarding the Abyssinian mainland, although Britain and France also advocate implementing an international mutual assistance plan, Italy seems to demand that it retain special influence in this mutual assistance system and that the Abyssinian Emperor be forced to accept this mutual assistance plan. The above are the opinions that Italy may raise on the Anglo-French proposals, but these formal proposals have not yet been sent to the Italian government, only informal news has been received from the Italian Embassy in France. (Havas, 10th)

International Commercial Telegrams

December 10th Reuters Special Commercial Telegram 83

Gold and Silver

British Gold: The London gold price today was 141 shillings and lost half a penny.

British Silver: The London silver price is not expected to be quoted until 4:15 PM at the earliest. The price may fall slightly due to a large number of sales. However, it is impossible to predict how much it will fall, as there is no news about Washington's attitude.

American Silver: The Mount Lyell silver price opened down about 200 pounds, due to a large number of sales, and there were no purchases from the United States in London.

Exchange Rates

British-American: The London foreign exchange market was stable this morning. The price of the pound has a slightly stronger trend. The opening price of the British-American exchange rate was 4.92875 yuan, 0.0125 lower than yesterday's American-British closing price. Within the first hour, it rose 0.000625, at noon it rose 0.0125, at 1 PM it rose another 0.0125, and at 2 PM it continued to rise 0.000625, reaching 4.9325 yuan.

British-French: The opening price was 74.75 francs, up 4 pounds. Within the first hour, it rose 3 pounds, at noon it rose 4 pounds, and at 2 PM it rose another 2 pounds, reaching 74.78 francs.

Cotton and Wheat

American Cotton: The New York cotton market did not move at the opening. Although the Liverpool market was loose, it did not affect the market price here. There was a slight upward trend after the opening, with traders buying, but operators remained hesitant, waiting for the Supreme Court's decision on the legality of handling fees. It is said that the American Cotton Public Storage Agency has a reserve of 900,000 bales, which is more than generally expected. This is also one of the reasons for the sluggish cotton market.

American Cotton: Liverpool cotton prices fell slightly, due to the extremely disappointing US government cotton production estimate released yesterday, and the news that the US cotton farmers' public storage agency's reserves were thicker than expected. At 1 PM, the January contract fell 11 pounds to 6.33.

British Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market was quiet this morning. Although the news of a large sale of Australian wheat to Japan before noon offset the disappointing news from overseas, the wheat price here this morning was still lower than yesterday. At 1 PM, the December contract price was 5 shillings and 11 pence, down 1.25 pence.

American Wheat: The Chicago wheat market fell slightly at the opening due to poor Liverpool telegrams, but the price quickly rebounded due to increased Australian wheat shipments to the Far East and purchases by flour manufacturers. The feed market was stable, with no price changes.

Rubber

London: London rubber opened stable. The April-June contract price did not move, remaining at 6.5 pence. At noon, it turned quiet, and the price loosened 0.0625 to 6.4375 pence.

New York: New York rubber fell slightly at the opening due to looser London telegrams, but the price stabilized after purchases by traders and speculators.

Securities

New York: The New York stock market had a very weak opening trend this morning. Many stocks that had risen sharply recently fell by more than one dollar. Copper and metal stocks were weak, automobile stocks loosened, railway stocks fell slightly, and public utility stocks, oil stocks, department stores, and entertainment stocks were stable. The Dow Jones 30 industrial stock average opened at 143.96, down 14 pounds. The prices are as follows:

Eastern Hebei Puppet Organization Intercepts Various Taxes 95

Tax Bureau and Unified Tax Bureau Occupied; Over 70,000 Yuan of Unified Tax Collected

Tianjin Correspondence: Since Yin Rugeng's betrayal, the magistrates and public security chiefs of the counties in eastern Luan have refused to join the rebellion. Those who managed to escape the war zone and report to the province, as well as those who could not escape, were forced to temporarily obey the puppet organization. However, they have not severed ties with the provincial authorities, and they still accept orders mailed from the province, but they record them in a separate book to distinguish them from the puppet Anti-Communist Committee. Those that do not conflict with the puppet organization are still followed, such as the evaluation committees of the counties, which were established under the orders of the province. The postal and telecommunications agencies in eastern Hebei have special commissioners stationed to inspect them. Recently, Ning County Magistrate Chen Zanyu secretly reported news to the province, which was discovered. The report was made to Zhang Yantian, the commander of the Second Security Brigade stationed at the Liushou Camp. When Chen disguised himself and accompanied two followers through the Liushou Camp, intending to board a car to Baoding to escape the scope of the puppet organization, he was intercepted and detained by Zhang's troops and reported to Yin Rugeng. Yin ordered Zhang to send someone to Tongxian for disposition. Seeing this, officials in other counties adopted a policy of self-preservation and dared not act rashly. The office of the Puppet Eastern Hebei Anti-Communist Autonomous Committee established in Tangshan is under the command of Yin Tixin, the director of the puppet office, and governs the territory under the jurisdiction of the former Eastern Hebei Administrative District Commissioner's Office. The tax collection agencies in the counties have all been seized. Yin also reorganized the Tangshan Unified Tax Management Office into the Puppet Eastern Luan Unified Tax Bureau, the Hebei Province Third District Tobacco and Alcohol License Levy Bureau into the Puppet Eastern Hebei Tobacco and Alcohol License Levy Bureau, and the Tangshan Tax Collection Bureau was expanded into the Puppet Eastern Luan Tax Collection Bureau. All original staff members of the tax bureaus were detained and forced to work. Therefore, since the 29th of last month, tax collection has begun. Among them, the unified tax alone has collected 60,000 to 70,000 yuan. The Tangshan unified tax includes the Kailuan coal tax, Qixin Cement Company cement tax, Huaxin Spinning Mill yarn tax, and Decheng Flour Company flour tax, totaling about 280,000 yuan per month. Among them, the Kailuan mine tax accounts for about 150,000 yuan, and the Qixin cement tax accounts for about 120,000 yuan. Since the puppet unified tax bureau began collecting taxes, the factories and companies have had to allow the puppet organization to levy taxes in order to maintain shipments. However, most of the Kailuan mine tax is directly paid to the Hebei-Chahar-Suiyuan-Shanxi Unified Tax Administration in Peiping. Those shipped outside the war zone still pay taxes in Peiping as before. Only those sold within the war zone have to pay taxes to the puppet organization. The Ministry of Finance previously ordered all personnel of the Tangshan Unified Tax Management Office to withdraw and work in Tianjin due to the occupation of the office, and ordered the Tianjin Unified Tax Management Office to assist in relocating tax collection. Recently, because all personnel of the Tangshan office were detained, and the factories and companies opposed re-levying taxes in a different location because they had already paid the unified tax within the Tangshan factory, this matter was not carried out. The Malan Valley and Gubeikou unified tax sub-cards have not yet been received by the puppet organization because there is no one available. Customs tax cards at other passes on the Great Wall are operating as usual. The puppet side has not interfered due to special relations. (8th)

Rigorous Rural Clearance in Eastern Shandong 96

Red Bandit Leaders Captured and Executed; Anti-Bandit Work in Various Counties Very Active

Weixian Correspondence: The Red Bandits in eastern Shandong are stirring. Han Fuqu, the chairman of the provincial government, sent Zhang Shutang's division to suppress them and telegraphed Chairman Chiang to report. It is said that Chairman Chiang's reply was received a few days ago, instructing them to quickly extinguish the flames and not allow them to spread. Recently, Han believed that although the bandits numbered several thousand, 90% were coerced civilians, and it would not be difficult to suppress them. Rural clearance is most important. He ordered Zhang Shutang to conscientiously carry it out. According to recent news of bandit suppression, in addition to the coerced civilians joining the bandits, the lurking bandits in the vicinity have also responded, using the names of the pseudo-China Shandong Red Army First Route Commander, Second Route Commander, and pseudo-Central Soviet Special Liaison Officer. Their base appears to still be located in more than a dozen villages at the junction of Muping and Haiyang counties, such as Tonghai Village, Wuji Village, Xia Village, Songjiao Village, and Duanjia Village. After Zhang Shutang convened a rural clearance meeting with the county magistrates in Laiyang a few days ago, he moved to Haiyang to command Zhao Tingbi's regiment to advance south from Muping. On the evening of the 4th of this month, Zhao's regiment suddenly surrounded villages such as Tonghai and Songjiao. Although the bandits resisted, their actual strength and guns were only several hundred. The rest were earthen guns and swords, so they were defeated like melting snow. The government troops recovered Tonghai Village. In addition to killing more than 30 bandits on the spot, more than 100 were captured alive and sent to Haiyang. Banners, official seals, and many books and leaflets inciting the people were also found. After Zhang interrogated the captured bandits, Wang Wenlan and Duan Chengzhai, the so-called Red Army commanders, were among them, as well as more than 20 female party members, all of whom confessed without denial. Zhang then telegraphed Han Fuqu. Han believed that the bandit leaders should be executed on the spot, and intellectuals should be killed without mercy. Those who were truly blindly following would be allowed to be released on bail. Therefore, their leaders have all been executed and their bodies are displayed on the main roads of Tonghai, Wuji, and other villages. Many of the female bandits had short hair, unbound feet, and modern clothes, which are not commonly seen in remote counties on weekdays. Tai Xinran, the director of the Shidao long-distance telephone bureau, also joined the bandits, and his guarantor has also been shot. Zhang Shutang has now moved from Haiyang to Xia Village to convene a meeting with the people and will inspect Wendeng County again in a few days. The road from Yantai to Xia Village was originally a motor road, but troops from the 81st Division are now stationed at various important stations. The Yantai Red Swastika Society has set out to provide relief in villages such as Tonghai. The remaining bandits scattered in various counties are being searched, and rural clearance is being actively carried out, with strict household registration checks. In addition to Zhang Shutang stationed in Xia Village and Zhao Tingbi's regiment stationed in Tonghai Village, Brigade Commander Yun Qichang is currently stationed in Rongcheng, and Brigade Commander Tang Bangzhi is currently stationed in Wendeng. Zhang Xiangwu, the commander of the Fifth Route Militia, was also ordered to assist in the suppression. Zhang arrived in Yantai from Pingdu on the 5th and immediately transferred to the territory of Qixia County. Also, since the 81st Division set off to suppress the bandits, the defense area of Qixia County that they left behind is now being taken over by Gu Liangmin's troops of the 22nd Division.

The anti-bandit situation in various counties in eastern Shandong is also very active at present. (1) Muping County: Brigade Commander Yun Qichang set off from Muping. He paid special attention to Songjiao Village, where the bandit leader Wang Wenlan was located, and Duanjia Village, where the bandit leader Duan Chengzhai was located. As for the bandits in various places, in addition to those killed on the spot, all those captured alive were interrogated, and if they belonged to a certain village, they were sent back to that village for execution to serve as a warning. The large group of bandits was defeated long ago and scattered in all directions. Gaoling Qujia in the southwest of the county was attacked by fleeing bandits again on the night of the 4th, who set fires to show their might. The villagers were confused and mostly fled to neighboring villages, and the situation was very chaotic. The number of bandits is still unclear. (2) Wendeng County: Slogans and leaflets were found in the county a few days ago, and the city gates were immediately closed with sand and soil, leaving only the east gate open for traffic, with extremely strict inspections to prevent accidents. Before long, bandits rioted in Guoge Village in the east of the city. The county magistrate ordered the Lian Zhuang Hui Ding to bravely encircle and suppress the bandits, killing several bandits before they fled. Now it is peaceful as usual. (3) Haiyang County: Guocheng, the fourth district of the county, is the most prosperous village. Recently, it planned to hold the anniversary of the establishment of the Jinde Branch Association. While preparations were underway, more than 40 bandits with complete guns surrounded the village a few days ago. The Lian Zhuang Hui closed the village gates to resist, and the Lian Zhuang Hui of nearby villages also came to rescue. They attacked from both inside and outside, and the bandits fled. Four bandits were killed and one was captured alive. Since hearing about the bandit riots, Dazhuang Xia Village in the east of the county has closed its doors, leaving only one door open for entry and exit. The Lian Zhuang Hui Ding is on guard day and night, and inspections of pedestrians are very strict. (4) Fushan County: County Magistrate Li Shusen, fearing that the bandit riots in various places would affect public security, ordered each of the five major districts to select 100 strong men. A few were left in the county seat for support, while the rest were assigned to defend each district. Because Shihuikouzi in the south of the port is an important avenue to Laiyang and Haiyang and has a relatively important location, in addition to stationing 20 to 30 people in the village, 80 people are stationed in Huangwu Village, 10 miles south, all under the command of Qu Shaofu, the head of the Second Lian Zhuang Branch Association. If the bandits flee north, they will be attacked head-on. (9th)

Jiading: Student Police Arbitrarily Arrest Vocational School Principal 97

The four towns of this city were ordered to carry out compulsory literacy education. Twenty literacy classes for the public were set up throughout the city and opened on the 5th of this month. Classes began on the night of the 6th. The county-run commercial vocational school independently managed one class. On the 6th and 7th, only a dozen students attended. According to regulations, the names of absent students were filled out on a form and sent to the town office, which then asked the Public Security Bureau to send police to force them to attend school. On the evening of the 8th, half an hour after class time had passed, only three students had arrived. Principal Pan Sigui telegraphed the town office to decide whether or not to hold class. The town office replied to dispose of it as appropriate, so he announced that class would be suspended today due to the small number of students. As the students were leaving, Wang Yifei, the squad leader of the student police class of the County Public Security Bureau, thought that the school should not dismiss the students who had been urged by the Public Security Bureau to attend class. He invited his classmates to return to the vocational school and rant at the school. Principal Pan explained the situation, but they ignored him. Then, he returned to the bureau and led a dozen classmates to guard the gates of the vocational school. Falsely claiming that it was the order of the director, they arrested Principal Pan. Pan asked for an arrest warrant, but the other police officers immediately stepped forward and forcibly dragged Pan into the bureau. The students in the literacy class at the school were also arrested and taken to the bureau. After entering the bureau, they privately beat Pan for about half an hour. Chen Youmin, the director of the bureau, returned to the bureau from outside and finally invited Pan into the reception room and said that the arrest was a false claim by Officer Wang and that there was no order. He apologized to Pan and said that he would severely punish Officer Wang and personally sent Pan back to school. The next morning, the education community heard the news that the student police of this county had repeatedly caused trouble illegally, causing public resentment. This time, they even falsely claimed an order and arbitrarily arrested the principal of a secondary school and illegally beat him within the bureau. The highest public security agency in the county had no discipline. At 1 PM, after gathering at the Educational Association, they elected 20 representatives, including Lü Yunbiao and Wang Xuanpu, to petition the county government for: (1) Punishing Officer Wang Yifei, who caused the incident illegally, dismissing him from public office, and never employing him again. (2) Severely punishing Public Security Director Chen Youmin for tolerating illegal police conduct. (3) Guaranteeing the safety of educators. County Magistrate Xu expressed his willingness to accommodate them. On the one hand, the teachers of various schools in this city who were teaching in the literacy classes jointly resigned to the town office. Town Chief Pu Juling tried his best to persuade them to stay and promised to be responsible for negotiating. At about 5 PM, County Magistrate Xu asked Huang Shizuo, the head of the first district, to report to the Educational Association that the first and second requests could be granted. The second request was changed to Director Chen apologizing in writing to the literacy education committee of the four towns, and he repeatedly asked the teachers to continue teaching. The teachers agreed to continue teaching for the time being to see what would happen. However, as of the time the reporter was writing the manuscript, the county government had not yet fulfilled the aforementioned items.

Wuxi: Fierce Woman Kills Two Sons and Then Commits Suicide 101

Ling Rongchang, a resident of Yingqiao Lane, in the city, worked in the Taibo Urban Area Office and was 37 years old. His second wife, Yao, was 32 years old and had two boys, the elder named Qiuquan, 3 years old, and the younger named Panquan, 2 years old. The couple often quarreled. The night before last (9th), Ling Rongchang went to Yingyetin in the suburbs to take a bath and did not return home until 11 PM. After entering the room, he saw that his two sons had blood flowing profusely from their necks, and Yao was also lying in a pool of blood. There was also a kitchen knife beside her head. He was extremely shocked and shouted loudly. He immediately asked Western doctor Wu Shisheng to come to his home for emergency treatment. The necks of the two children had been severed and they had already died. Yao was still breathing and was immediately sent to the Brothers Hospital for treatment. It is said that her throat had been severed. Hong Houchang, the director of the Public Security First Branch Bureau in charge of the area, heard the report and arrived at the scene. He briefly questioned Ling at the bureau and ordered him to return home, and sent police to guard Ling's home. At 10 AM yesterday, Huang Rongzhao, the head of the Northwest Third District, and Huang Bingjun, the head of the Northwest Fifth District, along with his colleagues, the owner Ling Rongchang, and his elder brother Shi Huang, went to the District Court to request an exemption from the autopsy. The Prosecutor's Office received the report and immediately sent Prosecutor Shen and clerks to conduct an autopsy on the bodies of Qiuquan and Panquan in the afternoon. It was determined that they had been killed by cutting while alive. The murder weapon was compared with the wounds and found to be consistent. The murder weapon was taken to the court for filing. Rongyu prepared coffins for the burial. Prosecutor Shen went to the Brothers Hospital to examine Yao before returning to the court.

Sentencing for Selling Poison Pills 102

The Inspectorate of the local Public Security Bureau arrested three people, Feng Genbao, Dai Bingxun, and Wu Gui, on November 8th of last year, at No. 2, Jingye Lane, for selling poison pills. Over a thousand poison pills were seized. They were presented to the county government and then transferred to the Zhenjiang Garrison Headquarters for interrogation. It is now known that Ren Yuan, the Chief of the Military Law Department of the Headquarters, has pronounced the sentences. Feng Genbao was sentenced to eight years of imprisonment for the crime of possessing narcotics with intent to sell. Dai Bingxun was sentenced to one year and six months of imprisonment for selling opium, with a fine of five hundred yuan. Wu Guiying was sentenced to four months of imprisonment for the crime of destroying evidence. Yesterday, all the above-mentioned criminals were sent back to the local county government to be sent to prison for execution of their sentences.

Sudden Cold Weather with Snowflakes Flying 103

Since the beginning of winter, the weather in our county has been erratic, sometimes cold and sometimes warm, sometimes rainy and sometimes sunny, resulting in frequent cases of colds and coughs. On the 8th of this month, the weather turned warm, with the temperature ranging from 30 to over 50 degrees on the thermometer. In the afternoon, there was a light drizzle that stopped in the evening. Yesterday morning (the 9th) at about 3 a.m., the northwest wind was very strong, with a roaring sound that shook the roof tiles. The weather turned cold, and the Fahrenheit thermometer dropped to 41 degrees. At about 8 a.m., snowflakes were flying, melting as soon as they hit the ground, and stopped at 11:30 a.m. However, the sky was covered with dense white clouds, suggesting the possibility of more heavy snow.

Xiao Jie, the head of Huaiqiao Township in the ninth district of Jiangdu, and Xiao Zhenyang, the head of the fourth bao, had long been at odds. Education Broadcasting Special Issue

Compulsory Education (1) 106

— Gu Shusen, Director of the General Education Department of the Ministry of Education

The topic I am talking about today is "Compulsory Education."

Before I begin, please think about what is called "Compulsory Education."

The meaning of so-called compulsory education is that the state uses law to stipulate that all people have an absolute obligation to provide their children or the children under their protection with education for a certain period of time within a certain age range. This is called compulsory education. This kind of law stipulates that people have the obligation to educate their children, and if they cannot comply, the government can enforce it according to law. Therefore, this kind of compulsory education is also called enforced education.

We might think, why does the state use law to stipulate that people must provide their children with a certain amount of education within a certain age? I think everyone can understand this meaning. It is because people become knowledgeable through education, their thinking becomes agile, their judgment of things becomes accurate, they understand etiquette, they understand the principles of being a person, and their personalities become noble. When people receive a certain amount of education in their childhood, they will naturally have a career when they grow up. Since they have a decent career in life, they will naturally be law-abiding and will not do evil. Then, the number of bad elements in society can be reduced, and society can be stabilized as a result. Furthermore, when education is popularized in a country, the knowledge of the people will naturally increase, and social undertakings will naturally develop. How can a country not be rich and strong? In short, to demand progress in people's knowledge, development in social undertakings, stability in order, and even the wealth and strength of the country, all depend on promoting compulsory education. Therefore, civilized countries around the world must use law to stipulate that people must provide their children with a certain amount of education.

According to what I said earlier: compulsory education is an obligation that people should fulfill to the country, and regardless of poverty or wealth, intelligence or stupidity, everyone should receive equal education. However, the scope of education is very broad, from kindergarten to elementary school, middle school, and even university. Everyone should have the opportunity to enjoy education. Then, the scope of compulsory education seems impossible to limit to elementary school. Regarding this point, if we only speak from the perspective of equal educational opportunities, or even the benefits of education for society and the country, of course, the wider the scope of compulsory education, the better. However, implementing education at all levels throughout the country requires huge expenses. Expanding the scope of compulsory education naturally requires more funding. Therefore, the first condition for the state to use law to define the scope of compulsory education must be to examine the economic capacity of the country and the people. Furthermore, if the scope of compulsory education is to be expanded, the length of time children spend in school receiving education must also be extended. If the living conditions of the general population in the country are very difficult, how can they afford to have their children receive education for a very long time? Therefore, the second condition for defining the scope of compulsory education must be to examine the living conditions of society and the people. In addition to these two conditions, the scope of compulsory education should not only be defined as very small and low at the beginning, but the time limit should also be very short. Later, after the implementation has had a certain effect, the scope should be gradually expanded and the time limit lengthened. Examining the results of compulsory education in various countries around the world, some started with very short time limits. Those with long time limits turned out to be implemented more slowly, while those with short time limits gradually increased the time limit and turned out to be faster. In short, the implementation of compulsory education must have a certain history before the level of education can be gradually improved and the time limit gradually lengthened. This is the second condition for defining the scope of compulsory education.

Now I can briefly report the general situation of compulsory education in various countries around the world for reference and comparison:

Germany was the first country to implement compulsory education. In 1619, the city of Weimar issued an order forcing citizens to send their children to school. Later, Gotha, Saxony, Bavaria, Baden and other places followed suit. In 1763, the Prussian king at the time, Frederick the Great, defeated France and Austria. He knew that compulsory education was very important, so he clearly stipulated compulsory school attendance measures. All Prussian citizens, from the age of five to thirteen or fourteen, who did not obey the order to attend school would have their parents or guardians fined. The implementation of compulsory education in Germany can be said to have been established at that time. In 1851, it was officially stipulated in the constitution. They defined the compulsory education period as eight years. The compulsory education funds used were raised locally, accounting for about eight-tenths, and government subsidies accounted for about two-tenths. After the European War, the government reorganized, local taxes were abolished, and all were changed to national taxes. As a result, all compulsory education funds were borne by the state. The level of compulsory education development in their country has reached its peak because of its long history, and everyone has received education. However, examining their past statistics: In 1894, the places where they had been implementing compulsory education for the longest time had a history of forty years. However, at that time, the statistics of the number of school-age children enrolled in schools nationwide only reached 33 percent. If we think about this carefully, this proves that if the compulsory education period is set too long, the effect of implementation will be relatively slow.

The motivation for France to implement compulsory education was launched in 1792. The initial compulsory school attendance period was set at three years. In 1887, after being defeated by Prussia, it formally stipulated compulsory measures, requiring all children aged six to thirteen to receive compulsory education and exempting them from tuition fees. Since then, their compulsory education has become more complete. After the European War, the school attendance period was changed to eight years. Since 1882, the compulsory education funds for their country have been such that the salaries of all elementary school teachers have been entirely borne by the central government, and the expenses borne by local areas are only sporadic expenses such as school repairs and student supplies. They have put a lot of effort into compulsory education facilities. However, there are still many illiterate people, as evidenced by the use of marks instead of signatures in marriage registration books, which shows that their compulsory education has not yet reached the highest level.

The compulsory education situation in England has always been biased towards freedom and development, so private schools are very developed. It was not until 1870 that a law was enacted to implement compulsory education, and the unified implementation of compulsory education can be said to have started at this time. The length of their compulsory education school attendance period has been set at nine years since the European War. The compulsory education funds borne by the central government have also increased to one-half since the European War, and the remaining one-half is still borne by local areas. Although the compulsory education period they stipulated is very long, and the unified and compulsory implementation is also very late, the foundation of past educational development is very solid, so now, nine years of compulsory education can be said to have been popularized.

Compulsory education in the United States was initially stipulated by the people of Massachusetts that parents had the obligation to send their children to school. It was not until 1825 that it was enacted by law and promoted throughout the province. Later, various provinces followed suit. According to a survey in 1927, there were already twenty provinces. Their compulsory education period varies from province to province. Most of them are from the age of seven to sixteen, and some provinces are only five years. Now, the average statistics of the number of enrolled children nationwide show that the number of enrolled children has reached 94 percent of school-age children. The compulsory education funds in their country are borne by the provincial governments, ranging from 20 to 60 percent. The central government also gives a large amount of official wasteland to local areas as a fund for compulsory education.

Japan began implementing compulsory education in 1872. Their school system stipulates that one elementary school district should be established for every 600 people, and children over the age of six must attend school. It was implemented simultaneously throughout the country. Their compulsory education funds have always been entirely borne by local governments. It was not until the seventh year of the Taisho era that the central government allocated funds for subsidies. The length of their compulsory education education period is six years, but in the first ten years or so, children only attended school for four months each year. Once sixteen months were satisfied, the education period was considered to have ended. Later, the number of days in school each year was gradually increased, and it was not until after the 33rd year of the Meiji era that it was uniformly required to be satisfied for four years.

Although the above-mentioned situations of the implementation of compulsory education in various countries are only five countries, it is enough for us to know the importance of urgently promoting compulsory education. We should all think deeply about why we should urgently promote compulsory education. Regarding this aspect, I also have to say a few words:

First, although our Chinese nation has a large population and a long history, perhaps because of the vast land and abundant resources and the obstruction of mountains and rivers, not only does each province have its own customs, habits, and languages, but even each county and each place has its own customs, habits, and languages. No wonder the people are gradually being divided and dispersed, like a plate of loose sand, difficult to unite. If we want to remedy this drawback, unite the national people and revitalize our inherent national spirit, we can only promote compulsory education, increase national awareness, improve closed customs, eliminate bad habits, and unify different languages to create a solid and united Greater Chinese nation. This is the first point of urgently needing to promote compulsory education.

Second, if we examine the most recent education statistics, we can know that the number of illiterate people accounts for more than 80 percent of the total population, and the number of enrolled children only accounts for 23 percent of the number of school-age children. We think that it is very difficult to train so many illiterate people to exercise their four rights, cultivate their political ability, and prepare them to be qualified as citizens. And the future illiterate people will be allowed to be produced in large numbers batch after batch. How terrible is this? Therefore, urgently promoting compulsory education, cultivating healthy future people, and cultivating them to be qualified as citizens is really a fundamental work.

Third, seeing the scene of declining production, rural bankruptcy, and the poverty of the people's livelihood in various parts of the country, I especially feel twelve points of fear. If we use the perspective of education to observe the root causes of why they have been caught in this situation, it is all because education is not widespread, so the people's production skills cannot be improved, and they are economically invaded by foreign countries, which leads to an irreversible situation. Therefore, although the current rescue plans must be planned, the fundamental method relies entirely on the power of education to remedy it. In this way, promoting compulsory education is really urgently needed.

The three points mentioned earlier are the major reasons why we urgently need to promote compulsory education. There is also a need to report on the process of our country's promotion of compulsory education, the status of the implementation of compulsory education in various provinces and cities this year, and the opinions on promoting compulsory education, which I will talk about next time.

Effectiveness of the New Currency Policy, Gold and Silver are Concentrated and Transported to Shanghai, More Than 6,000 Taels of Gold are Transported from Fujian and Jiangxi, More Than 1.6 Million Silver Dollars in Xiamen 115

According to the East China News Agency, since the implementation of the new currency policy, not only has the turnover of funds in cities become easier, but even remote provinces have begun to use legal tender. Many provinces have also transported gold and silver to Shanghai to exchange for legal tender. The East China News Agency reporter learned the following information:

Cash Transported from Fujian and Jiangxi Provinces

After the Ministry of Finance issued an order to implement the new currency system, the provinces of Fujian and Jiangxi immediately notified all sectors to comply with the order. Jiangxi Province had previously collected more than 1,800 taels of gold from various gold shops and transported them to exchange for legal tender. Xiamen also transported cash of more than 4,400 taels and more than 1.6 million silver dollars to exchange for the legal tender of the three banks.

Subsidiary Currency Needed in Gansu and Sichuan Provinces

Sichuan is the largest province in our country with a large population. After Liu Hangchen, Director of the Sichuan Finance Department, borrowed 12 million from the Bank of China, the Ministry of Finance has agreed to provide financial assistance. It is now known that the province's greatest need is one-yuan new currency and subsidiary currency notes. The three banks have been providing as much assistance as possible. As for Gansu Province, it has repeatedly telegraphed the Ministry of Finance to transport new currency notes. Recently, the Ministry of Finance has also transported more than 2 million yuan in one-yuan notes and fractional currency for use.

Financial Activities in Tianjin and Jinan

As for Shandong and Hebei provinces, the financial circles of the cities have jointly complied with the Ministry of Finance's order to revive the market. In Jinan, the banking industry has released 1.9 million yuan in loans and the money industry has released 100,000 yuan in loans, totaling 2 million yuan, to assist industry and commerce. In Tianjin, the Hebei Provincial Bank has temporarily issued 200,000 yuan in copper coin bills. After the bank designated by the Ministry of Finance issues copper coin notes, it will be recalled and destroyed.

Repayment of Austrian Indemnity and Nine Other Public Bonds: Lottery Held Yesterday Morning; Total Repayment of $4,385,000; Payment for Austrian Bonds on the 20th, Remaining Bonds at Month's End 116

The lottery for the repayment of principal of the Austrian Indemnity and nine other public bonds was held at 10:00 AM yesterday at the Bankers' Club on Hong Kong Road. The total repayment amount is $4,385,000. Attendees included Chiang Lü-fu, Director of the Public Debt Department of the Ministry of Finance; Lin Chin-tzu, Supervisor from the Auditing Department; Hsu Chi-ching from the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce; Fan Chieh-tang from the National Debt Fund Management Committee; Wu Wei-ju from the Shanghai Banking Association; Shen Ching-liang from the Shanghai Money Trade Association; Chin Wen-yuan from the Central Bank, Chu Chi-chen from the Bank of China; Chen Hsuan from the Bank of Communications; Ho Hsiao-chuan, Tsung Po-hsuan, and Liang Yao-tsung, Administrators; Yu Tun-ti, Chi Chun-tsai, and Fang Ching-chung, Recorders; Wang Huai-fen, Huang Chi-tsung, and Ling Chi-chun, Clerks; Huang Mei-chien, Document Officer; Kung Pao-chen, Cheng I-chien, Chen Chien, and Hsu Pang-cheng, Receptionists; and over forty other individuals.

Chairman's Report

Chiang Lü-fu reported, "Today, we are holding the lottery for the repayment of principal for nine public bonds, including the Austrian Indemnity Secured 24 Treasury Notes, etc. The lottery method will continue to use two sets of numbers. Now, I will briefly report on the circumstances of each bond: (1) The Austrian Indemnity Secured 24 Treasury Notes were issued in 1926, with a total value of $2,400,000. Principal has already been repaid nineteen times. This is the twentieth repayment. Two bonds will be drawn, with a repayment amount of $48,000. (2) The 6% Public Bond of 1918 was issued with a total value of $45,000,000. Principal has already been repaid twenty-three times. This is the twenty-fourth repayment. One bond will be drawn, with a repayment amount of $450,000. (3) The Public Bond of 1925 was issued with a total value of $15,000,000. Principal has already been repaid twenty-three times. This is the twenty-fourth repayment. Eight bonds should be drawn, but since this is the final repayment, no lottery is necessary. The total repayment is $1,200,000. (4) The Military Expenditure Public Bond of the Ministry of Finance of the National Government was issued in 1928, with a total value of $10,000,000. Principal has already been repaid nineteen times. This is the twentieth repayment. Two bonds will be drawn, with a repayment amount of $192,000. (5) The Rehabilitation Short-Term Public Bond of the Ministry of Finance of the National Government was issued in 1928, with a total value of $40,000,000. Principal has already been repaid twenty-two times. This is the twenty-third repayment. Two bonds will be drawn, with a repayment amount of $800,000. (6) The 1929 Disaster Relief Public Bond was issued with a total value of $10,000,000. Principal has already been repaid twenty-one times. This is the twenty-second repayment. Two bonds will be drawn, with a repayment amount of $200,000. (7) The 1930 Customs Revenue Public Bond was issued with a total value of $20,000,000. Principal has already been repaid nineteen times. This is the twentieth repayment. One bond will be drawn, with a repayment amount of $195,000. (8) The 1934 Customs Revenue Public Bond was issued with a total value of $10,000,000. Principal has already been repaid once. This is the second repayment. One bond will be drawn, with a repayment amount of $1,000,000. (9) The 1935 Telegraph Administration Public Bond was issued with a total value of $10,000,000. This is the first repayment. Three bonds will be drawn, with a repayment amount of $300,000. Payments for the above drawn bonds, including principal and accrued interest, for the 24 Treasury Notes are scheduled for December 20th, and the remaining eight public bonds are scheduled for December 31st. Payments will be made through the Central, China, and Communications Banks in various locations. Please ask the supervisors to verify the drawn bonds and stubs in order to proceed with the lottery."

Drawn Numbers

After the Chairman's report, the supervisors verified the bonds and stubs, and then proceeded with the lottery. The drawn numbers are listed below: (1) Austrian Indemnity Secured 24 Treasury Notes: Two bonds, "No. 33" and "No. 61." (2) 6% Bond of 1918: One bond, "No. 92." (3) 1925 Bond: Eight bonds, "No. 04," "No. 41," "No. 44," "No. 50," "No. 66," "No. 70," "No. 82," and "No. 85." (4) Military Expenditure: Two bonds, "No. 75" and "No. 35." Silver Trade Association Re-submits Request to Ministry of Finance Regarding Silver Usage, Chemical Silver is No Different From Artificial Silk, Fu Sheng-mao Speaks Out on its Evils 120

Kuo Wen News Agency reports that the Silver Trade Association of this city has yesterday specially resubmitted a request to the Ministry of Finance regarding the silver usage issue in the industry, the original submission reads, this request concerns the silver usage management regulations, which have caused obstacles in both the work and business of the silver trade, in accordance with the provisions of Article 11, we request permission to continue to use silver with a purity of 88 percent, please approve the filing. Your humble association submitted a request to the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce last month, which was forwarded to your ministry, to allow the silver trade to continue to manufacture with the old composition percentage in accordance with the provisions of Article 11 of the management regulations, and we have been waiting patiently until now without any instructions. The members of your association are in a state of trepidation. If the regulations promulgated by the ministry can be followed with some effort, your members, although merchants, would not dare to lag behind others in patriotism, and would not repeatedly urge you. In fact, the silver trade has always been named after silver, and the manufacture of ornaments should be based on silver. If copper seven and silver three are used as raw materials, the nature of the product will be very hard, and it will easily break when struck. The silver trade is limited by manual techniques, and it is difficult to create good products. Moreover, the ministry has stipulated that chemical silver should be used as raw material, but our country does not have this kind of quality, and if we seek to purchase it from foreign countries, funds will have to flow out again, so saving money will turn into outflows. Your ministry's restriction on the silver content of silverware is intended to prevent the leakage of silver abroad, but our industry, in addition to manufacturing various utensils and ornaments, does not sell raw silver. The manufacture of utensils and ornaments requires labor costs and decoration fees for each tael of silver, which is about three or four yuan in legal tender. There are also the joint guarantee in Article 5 of the same rules and the punishment rules in Article 9. Since there is no profit to be made, even the most foolish person would never do this illegal thing. Moreover, although the silver products are taken from the country, they are actually scattered among the people, circulating back and forth, and still do not leave the country. People who hold them can redeem or pawn them in times of emergency, and can buy or redeem them in times of affluence, and the livelihoods of hundreds of thousands of silver trade workers can be maintained. If there is no flow of silver products in our country, imported goods will inevitably replace them, and in the future, what is distributed among the people will all be imported goods, and the outflow of rights and interests can be imagined. Observing the seizure of the porcelain industry and the invasion of the silk industry, major impacts have occurred on the country and industry and commerce. Today's so-called chemical silver is no different from artificial silk. Therefore, the members of your association unanimously appeal, requesting the minister to think of the livelihoods of hundreds of thousands of industrial and commercial people, and quickly approve the use of silver regulations Article 11 "but the book" stipulates, still containing 88% pure silver, to approve the filing, so that commerce can be maintained, workers will not lose their jobs, without harm to the country and benefit to the people, I beg the minister to observe and approve the implementation, it is convenient for the public, respectfully presented to the Minister of Finance Kong."

The reporter visited Mr. Fu Shengmao, chairman of the association, yesterday and conducted the following Q&A. Reporter asks, (hereinafter referred to as question) When did the silver trade begin? Mr. Fu replied, (hereinafter referred to as answer) The silver trade began in the Jin and Tang dynasties, so our industry has a slogan: "Tang makeup, Jin decoration." At that time, jewelry was the main body, and the Ming and Qing dynasties were the most prosperous. In recent times, there have been utensils, dressing tables, etc., and since the Republic of China, gifts have been the most important. (Question) How much silver does the silver trade use each year? (Answer) In the past three years, the average number of pulls has been about 400,000 taels of pure silver each year, but this is limited to members of the association. The number of silver shops that have not joined the association is several hundred, and the amount of silver used is about the same as that of the members. (Question) Can silver products be profited by transporting them out of the country? (Answer) The labor cost of silver products is very large. Once it becomes a vessel, labor costs and decoration fees must be added. Each tael of silver is at least about three or four yuan in legal tender. Not only is there no profit to be made, but also losses are many. (Question) Then, is the raw material that has not been made into a vessel sold? (Answer) The silver trade has never sold silver ingots as raw materials. It is safe to operate a business and strictly abide by the law. The members of the current trade association are willing to abide by Article 5 of the Finance Department's Management Regulations to jointly and severally guarantee and take joint responsibility. (Question) Are there any foreign silver factories? (Answer) There are silver manufacturing plants in various countries in the East and West. The products are mainly wine utensils, tea utensils and tableware, followed by display items, and then jewelry. The products are mainly plain, and delicate patterns are rare, because they all use electric machines instead of manual labor. Now, jewelry in our country is also decreasing year by year, which is related to the impact of women cutting their hair. (Question) What is the composition of foreign silverware? (Answer) The silver content of foreign silverware is about 70 percent, but our industry never accepts exchanges, because there is no deep experience, and we are especially afraid of causing disputes. (Question) What exactly is the so-called chemical silver? (Answer) Our industry is sticking to the old ways and does not know what chemical silver is. Moreover, our country does not have this kind of raw material now, otherwise, we can only purchase it from foreign firms, and then funds will have to flow out, and it is not suitable for the technical raw materials of handicrafts. (Question) If the silver trade does not manufacture utensils, is there a possibility that imported goods will replace them? (Answer) If our industry does not produce silver utensils, imported products of so-called chemical silver will take the opportunity to enter, win by surprise, and sell as much as possible, subtly changing habits, and once they become old, they will become waste. There will be a huge leak, and the country and the people will suffer. Looking at the porcelain industry and the silk industry, they have become the master of the house. Can we not be filled with emotion? Chemical silver is no different from artificial silk. Once it is harmed, it is impossible to stop. It is saving money but making it overflow. (Question) Now the Ministry of Finance stipulates that the pure silver content of silver products is 30 percent. Can it be made? (Answer) If it is based on the provisions of Article 2 of the Finance Department's Silver Usage Regulations, it is impossible to work, because copper seven and silver three, its nature becomes hard, our industry is completely made by hand, and once struck, it will inevitably be broken, its color cannot be white, and the issue of credibility is even more unnecessary. Therefore, the silver trade across the country has requested the Ministry of Finance to amend Article 2 of the Management Regulations and requested the approval of Article 11 "but the book". This association has also submitted two requests to the Ministry of Finance, but has not yet received approval. (Question) What is the relationship between the silver trade and the national parties? (Answer) The foundation of a country is stable, depending on whether industry and commerce are developed or not. In all countries, the business is to lead the way, and our country is called a country based on agriculture, and it is also heard to promote industry and commerce recently. Our industry is one of the industries that attach importance to both industry and commerce. Although there is no possibility of selling to foreign countries, it is also enough to settle the people's livelihood in one industry in the country. Production and sales, huge capital, its raw materials are taken from the country, (now allowed to supply the central bank) and scattered among the people, circulating back and forth, does not leave the country, gold is also silver, once it enters the people, it becomes a kind of small savings, which can be exchanged and pawned in times of emergency, and purchased and redeemed in times of affluence, directly and indirectly hundreds of thousands of workers rely on it to maintain their lives, the country has no unemployed people, and society has no hungry and cold people, so our industry is actually beneficial and harmless to the people of both countries.

Page 10

China Giant Airplane Delivers Chinese Mail to Shanghai; Only Two Weeks from the United States to Shanghai 124

The United States has opened the Far East route. The giant airplane named 'China' has crossed the Pacific from the United States and flown to the Philippines, thus opening the route. The first batch of Chinese mail carried by this aircraft arrived in Shanghai on the 9th, transferred from the Dollar Line's President Jackson. According to the postmark dates, it took seven days from San Francisco to the Philippines and seven days from the Philippines to Shanghai. The total time for mail delivery from the United States to Shanghai was only two weeks, which is two weeks shorter than the previous delivery time entirely by ship. Unified Text Telegraph Regulations; Officially Implemented on the First Day of Next Month; Ministry of Communications Instructs Telegraph Bureaus to Comply 126

In order to expedite the sending and receiving of military and political telegrams and improve the operations of various bureaus, the Ministry of Communications has drafted seven articles of unified text telegraph regulations and submitted them to the National Government for instructions to all military and political agencies to comply starting from January 1 of next year. Yesterday, the Telegraph Bureau in this city was ordered to comply. A reporter from the Industrial News Agency inquired about the regulations from the bureau yesterday: (1) Telegrams with the same text sent to multiple receiving locations are called unified text telegrams. (2) The names of the locations in a unified text telegram cannot be listed together. Each telegram can only contain one receiving location. If telegrams are sent to multiple locations, they should be divided into multiple copies. (3) When a unified text telegram is submitted to the telegraph bureau for transmission, only one copy needs to contain the complete text. The remaining copies can specify the receiving location and the name and address of the recipient on the bottom of the telegram, and indicate "One telegram is the same as Telegram No. X to Location Y," without needing to include the complete text. (4) For circular telegrams intended for the recipients to be aware of, the fee-paying service mark "Circular" or "Circular" should be added before each receiving location name. (5) For non-circular telegrams intended to inform the recipient that the telegram is also being sent to a certain person in a certain location, the phrase "In addition to being sent to Person A in Location B" should be stated in the text. (6) If a telegram is sent to multiple people in the same location, the method of sending multiple copies should still be followed, indicating "Send X copies," without needing to be divided into multiple copies like a unified text telegram. (7) These regulations are submitted by the Ministry of Communications to the Executive Yuan for submission to the National Government for instructions to comply.

Directors and Supervisors of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Abandon Their Intention to Resign; Awaiting Reorganization 130

All the directors and supervisors of the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company had previously submitted written resignations to the Ministry of Communications, which were then submitted to the Executive Yuan, citing financial exhaustion and operational difficulties. International Labor Office Notifies Arrival in Shanghai; International Labor Conference to Be Held Next June 131

The Chinese branch of the International Labor Office in this port received a notice from the ILO headquarters in Geneva yesterday, informing them that the 20th International Labor Conference will be held in Geneva on June 4 next year (1936). The important agenda includes the following eight items: (1) Regulations on several special worker recruitment systems; (2) The issue of paid leave; (3) Reduction of working hours in public works undertaken or subsidized by the government; (4) Reduction of working hours in the construction industry and civil engineering; (5) Reduction of working hours in the steel industry; (6) Reduction of working hours in the coal mining industry; (7) Reduction of working hours in the textile industry; (8) The issue of safety for construction workers. In addition to discussing the report of the Director of the International Labor Office, reviewing the annual reports of various governments on the implementation of conventions, the report on the implementation of the Convention on Equal Treatment for Injury Compensation, and amending the rules of the conference, it will also be necessary to listen to the International Labor Office's reports on collective agreements, the recruitment and introduction of immigrant workers, and opium and labor.

City Land Bureau's Reply: Assisting the Court in Executing Land Cases 132

Complete Processing Within Ten Days of Document Receipt; Separate Orders Issued to Local Land Guards to Exert Their Utmost Efforts

The Shanghai Lawyers' Association yesterday issued a notice to all members, stating: "Respected sirs, previously, member Xu Zuoliang proposed that in this city, land is sometimes auctioned by court order due to debt. The Standing Committee of the Court often requests the City Land Bureau to estimate the land value as a standard for execution and auction. However, the City Land Bureau's valuation often takes three to five months, or even a year, which is far slower than the valuation speed of the Shanghai Municipal Council (SMC) in the concessions. Furthermore, when inquiring about land map and guarantee numbers from local land guards, the land guards often create difficulties and extort money, causing great suffering to litigants. It is proposed to forward a letter to the City Land Bureau, requesting that in the future, when entrusted with estimating land value, they should order their subordinates to complete the process swiftly within two weeks, and instruct all local land guards to immediately provide the requested land map and guarantee numbers when inquired, to facilitate execution, etc." It was felt that Mr. Xu's proposal was insightful, and a letter was forwarded to the Shanghai City Land Bureau, requesting its adoption. Now, a reply has been received, stating: "The letter of November 19th is acknowledged, 'Regarding cases where the court requests land valuation, please complete the estimation within two weeks, and please instruct all land guards to provide accurate information when inquired about land map and guarantee numbers,' etc. Upon review, matters regarding land valuation requested by the courts in this city are handled according to the procedures stipulated by this bureau. Except for cases involving occupied land that require prior measurement, or where the reported map, embankment, and lot numbers are incorrect, or where the location is unclear, requiring summoning land guards for separate inquiries and boundary demarcation, and cases involving separate disputes over single deeds, which are temporarily difficult to complete within a limited time, all matters will be processed within ten days of document receipt. As for the request to instruct the land guards, it has been complied with. A reply is hereby issued for your information." This has been discussed and resolved at the 213th Joint Meeting of the Executive and Supervisory Committees of this Association, and all members are hereby notified for their information."

Loan Committee: Continued Disbursement of Industrial and Commercial Credit Loans; Over 34,000 Yuan Approved at Yesterday's Meeting 134

The Shanghai Industrial and Commercial Loan Review Committee held its 18th meeting yesterday at the China National Goods Bank. The attending committee members included Cai Zengji, Qin Runqing, Yu Zuoting (substituting for Qin Runqing), Song Ziliang, Wang Xiaolai, Du Yuesheng, Chen Guangfu (substituting for Wang Xiaolai), Bei Songsun, Wang Yansong, etc. Committee members Xi Demao and Zhang Peishen were excused. Chairman Cai Zengji reported on routine committee affairs. Fifty-seven applications for industrial and commercial credit small loans were submitted. After review and discussion, it was decided to approve loans for two companies, reduce the loan amount for twenty-five companies, grant half of the original loan amount to nineteen companies, and reject eleven companies. A total of 34,850 yuan was approved. The committee will notify the applicants of the decisions separately. It is reported that most of those whose loan applications were rejected were because their businesses did not deal in national goods, or because the loan purpose did not comply with the loan regulations. According to the committee's loan principles, loans are limited to factories that manufacture national goods, merchants who sell national goods, and those who transport national goods for export. These industrial and commercial credit loans are still being processed. Those who meet the above principles can obtain application forms at the committee's office on the second floor of the National Goods Bank on Tianjin Road and apply according to the regulations.

Rent Reduction United Federation: Actively Carrying Out Rent Reduction Work 137

Since rumors arose in this city, residents in the Zhabei and North Sichuan Road areas have moved away, causing landlords who relied on sub-renting to third-party tenants to supplement their income to suddenly feel an unbearable burden. The matter of tenants in Sida Lane on Shigaota Road requesting a two-month rent reduction from the landlord has already been reported in the newspapers. Following that, tenants at Heng'an Lane, Dade Lane, Xinxiang Lane, and Yongfeng Lane on North Sichuan Road have also made the same request. This is indeed a serious problem amidst the economic downturn. The details of the situation are as follows: (1) Tenants in Dade Lane, Heng'an Lane, Yongfeng Lane, and Xinxiang Lane joined the Shanghai All-Tenants Rent Reduction United Federation and organized the First Branch to carry out rent reduction campaigns due to the unbearable pressure of high rents. Recently, due to rumors arising in this city, three-fifths of the residents in Dade Lane have moved away, only one-fourth of those in Yongfeng Lane remain, and less than half in Xinxiang Lane. Those who have not moved are only small landlords who are guarding empty houses. Once the third-party tenants move away, no one cares about the remaining houses. They are unable to bear the entire rent, and the landlords will not allow them to default. Therefore, all four tenants convened a meeting of all tenants at the Zhongshan Fellow Villagers Association on the 8th of this month, guided by federation representatives Mr. Peng and Mr. Zhu, and unanimously passed a request that the methods of rent reduction and exemption should follow previous lane precedents. The meeting issued a letter to the landlords of the four lanes, urging them to give a satisfactory reply as soon as possible. (2) Tenants Song Weirong, Ye Zufan, Tao Jiafu, Ji Housheng, etc. in Yuqing Lane on Gonghe Road in Zhabei stated that the monthly rent for the houses in the lane before the 20th year of the Republic of China was 15 yuan. After slightly renovating them in January of the 21st year of the Republic of China, the rent was increased significantly. Now, with the market downturn, they are unable to bear the burden. Therefore, they and the rent reduction federation representative Zhuo Wen went to the landlord Xie Fuqing the other day to make a request for a 40% rent reduction. Unexpectedly, the landlord refused their request. Currently, all tenants in the lane have deposited their rent in the bank and have unanimously stopped paying to urge the landlord to come to his senses. (3) All tenants in Kenye Lane on Oujia Road joined the Shanghai All-Tenants Rent Reduction United Federation and organized the Ninth Branch. The inaugural meeting was held the other day, guided by federation representative Zhuo Wen. Zhou Tianping, Tian Yide, and others were elected as executive committee members on the spot. The branch had previously sent a letter to Kenye Bank requesting a rent reduction, but has not yet received a reply. Therefore, on the 8th of this month, another meeting of all tenants was convened, and it was decided that from this month onwards, they would unanimously stop paying rent until a satisfactory reply was received.

Lu Shunxing of Lao Bei Men Carelessly Set Fire; Six Men and Women Tragically Buried in Flames; Rumored to Have Started from a Beggar Warming Himself by a Fire Late at Night; Disasters Befell Neighbors with Material Losses of 8,000 Gold 151

Lu Shunxing Mingwa (Skylight Tile) Store at No. 17 Yan Hai Road, Lao Bei Men, suddenly caught fire on the ground floor at 2:30 AM yesterday. The skylight tiles in the store were easily flammable, causing the flames to rise fiercely and become unapproachable. After the police on duty reported to the fire brigade, three fire engines were immediately dispatched from the Southern District and the French Concession to put out the fire. It took half an hour to extinguish the fire, but the entire Lu Shunxing store had been reduced to ashes. The floor of its neighbor, Zhang Fachang Round Wood Store at No. 15, was also destroyed. After investigation, it was found that only the mistress of the Lu Shunxing residence, Mrs. Lu Zhang, a native of Pudong, and two apprentices, Lu Lingeng, 17 years old, local natives, escaped. The rest, including the young master Lu Rongsheng and his wife, their two sons, the mother-in-law, and the old steward, totaling six people, were buried in the flames. After the fire was extinguished, the bodies found at the fire scene were all charred and their faces were blurred and unrecognizable, which was a terrible sight. They were sent to the Xiying Public Office in the Southern City. The local court sent personnel to inspect them at noon. The corpses were to be coffined and buried. The fire was caused by a fire along the street, burning from bottom to top. It is rumored that a vagrant burned paper to warm himself late at night, which spread to the skylight tiles and bamboo tips piled up in front of the door. In particular, the fire broke out at the staircase inside the door. When the fire spread, the staircase broke, and the people sleeping upstairs could not escape, resulting in being burned to death. Lu Shunxing's business was barely enough to make a living. They originally had fire insurance, but it expired in July of this year. In order to save money, the young master Lu Rongsheng cancelled the insurance. His mother-in-law, Zhu Tang, was the sister-in-law of the Zhu family, the owner of the round wood store at No. 11. She had just recovered from an illness in her hometown and was specially invited to Shanghai to recuperate, but she was buried in the fire. Lu's two sons, one was only four years old, named Mao Tou, and the other was only two years old, named Zhixiang. The old steward, Chen Chengqian, was nearly sixty years old and had worked at the store for many years. He also failed to escape this time. Yesterday, the mistress Lu Zhang and apprentice Lu Lingeng were questioned by the Lao Bei Men Police Station and then released. The total material loss of houses and other things is estimated to be around 8,000 gold, which is the most tragic disaster in the Southern District this year. In other news, the six corpses that were burned to death have been transported by car to the Xiying Public Office on Liu Fen Road. Shen Zhenhua, the chief of the Lao Bei Men Police Station in charge, ordered the local security officer to report to the Shanghai Local Court and asked them to send personnel to the scene for inspection before ordering them to coffin them separately. The cause of the fire is currently under strict investigation by the police station.

Maochang Glasses Company Catches Fire; Huili Clothing Store Also Affected; Vehicles Stopped, Resembling a Long Snake

A fire broke out at the intersection of Nanjing Road and Yunnan Road yesterday morning, and traffic was also blocked. The details are as follows:

The Maochang Glasses Company at the intersection of Nanjing Road and Yunnan Road suddenly caught fire at 8:15 AM yesterday morning, just as it was opening for business. Traffic Jam

At the same time, traffic on Xizang Road, Laohai Road, Yunnan Road, Guizhou Road, and other roads near the Nanjing Road intersection was temporarily blocked. Dismissal of a Manager Named Wang Enrong for Misconduct; Rejected Appeal of a Murder Conviction; Heinous Crime Deserves Death 154

Wang Enrong, a 29-year-old Tianjin native, previously served as a manager at the Great World amusement park. After being dismissed for misconduct in August of this year, Wang harbored resentment towards Wang Dekui, a Yancheng native and the deputy chief inspector of the amusement park. On the evening of September 19th, Wang concealed two sharp, double-edged knives and sneaked into the Great World, stabbing Wang Dekui in vital areas with two blows. Wang Dekui was sent to the hospital but died despite treatment. After the incident, Wang Enrong went to the main entrance of the Great World, where he was apprehended by detectives who recovered the murder weapon and brought him back to the police station. The police department filed a public prosecution for murder. After the trial, Wang Enrong was sentenced to life imprisonment and permanent deprivation of his civil rights. The defendant, dissatisfied with the verdict, appealed to the Higher Third Branch Court. Wang Yue, a judge of the High Court, repeatedly opened investigative hearings and examined the reasons for Wang's appeal, in which he falsely claimed that the victim died because of an incision in his abdomen during the hospital operation, attempting to reduce his guilt. This has been previously reported in this newspaper. The case was then reviewed by the High Court collegial panel, and yesterday at 3:00 PM, acting presiding judge Sun Honglin, accompanied by judges Wang and Qiu, came to the Third Criminal Court and ordered the appellant Wang Enrong to be brought to the case. The appeal was rejected, and the presiding judge explained the reasons for the judgment in summary to the defendant, stating that because he committed misconduct and was dismissed, he harbored resentment towards his superior and stabbed the victim to death, which he had admitted. He could not claim that the death was due to negligence during the hospital operation. An investigation revealed that the victim suffered serious injuries and the hospital provided legal treatment, all of which are documented. The investigation into the defendant's crime revealed that the circumstances were particularly heinous. Sentencing him to death according to the law would not be excessive. The original trial sentenced him to life imprisonment, which was already lenient. His further appeal was deemed to be completely without merit, so the appeal was rejected and the original judgment was upheld. If he was not satisfied, he could submit a statement to this court within ten days after receiving the judgment to appeal to the Supreme Court. The defendant, after being advised, still sought leniency and a reduced sentence. The official advised him that the judgment had been made and that he should not speak further. The defendant then lowered his head and remained silent, and was led away by the bailiffs back to the detention center.

Permanent Incapability of Straightening Up; Ren Xiangyun Returned to Custody, Others Released on Bail
