Chinese Detective Jin Wanrong Awarded for Distinguished Service 157

Jin Wanrong, Chinese Detective No. 60 of the Public Concession Police Department, has been awarded the First Class Medal for Distinguished Service and his meritorious service recorded by the Concession Police Department’s Honours Committee, after being proposed by the Municipal Council Board for extraordinary loyalty and bravery and meritorious service in capturing thieves. It is reported that at approximately 7:00 PM on the evening of July 2nd of this year, the Yulin Road Police Station received a report that four robbers were dining at No. 156 Pingliang Road and dispatched Chinese and Western detectives to surround and arrest them. Upon reaching the location, they rushed in through the back door. Jin Wanrong, holding a gun, bravely led the way up the stairs. At that time, the four robbers were dining and immediately opened fire to resist arrest upon seeing the detectives. Jin was hit first and fell to the ground with a wound to his right waist. Behind Jin, Western Detective Granville and Chinese Detective No. 98 fired inwards at the doorway. Bullets flew everywhere, and two robbers fell in response. When Granville and No. 98 ran out of bullets, they went downstairs to reload. One robber then fled to the sun deck to escape, but was spotted by Chinese Detective No. 104, who had arrived and saw the fleeing robber from the adjacent room’s sun deck and shot him down. At this time, only Jin Wanrong was fighting two robbers in the room. Jin was already injured, but still thought of making the arrest, which caused him to be shot in the right leg. When Jin ran out of bullets and had no time to reload, he thought of seizing the gun from the injured robber. The injured robber fired another shot at Jin, fortunately missing. Jin then used his strength to subdue him and seize his weapon. At that moment, another robber fired a shot that penetrated Jin's body. Jin had already been shot three times. At this time, the robber who had fired two shots was still uninjured and immediately jumped onto the balcony to escape, but was spotted by detectives outside the door, who immediately shot him down. Jin, having seized the enemy's weapon in the room, immediately found a way to shoot down one robber and seized the weapon of the other robber. Thus, all four robbers were captured. Jin saw that the matter was over and crawled up, thinking of going downstairs alone, but collapsed at the doorway, unable to support himself due to his serious injuries. He was then supported down by other detectives and taken to the hospital for treatment. The police department later praised Jin for his meticulousness in the face of danger, commendable loyalty and bravery, and his ability to subdue three robbers after suffering serious injuries. They unanimously expressed admiration and awarded him the First Class Medal for Distinguished Service.

Notorious Female Gangster Gu Jindi Arrested 158

Exposed for Selling Red Pills; Sentenced to Two Years in Prison After Trial

There are two well-known female gangsters in this city: one is Lu Laoqi, and the other is Gu Jindi, the sister of the former Flower Association King Zheng Meitang. Both have extraordinary influence, with many followers. Recently, Lu was arrested by the French Concession Police for suspicion of involvement in an assassination case and sent to the Second Special District Court for interrogation and detention. Gu was also arrested by the Hongkou Police for trafficking red pills. Thus, these two notorious female leaders of Shanghai have both been caught in the legal net. The details of Gu's arrest are as follows:

Gu Jindi, a Ningbo native, 30 years old. After her brother Zheng Meitang was killed, she married a gangster named Gu and lived with him at No. 21, Lane 122, Yuanfang Road. She took her husband's surname. Last year, Gu was sentenced to ten years in prison by the First Special District Court for murder. He then appealed to the Second Branch of the High Court and was acquitted due to insufficient evidence. Gu Jindi, on the other hand, has special influence in the Hongkou area and secretly runs a red pill business, using women to transport them to avoid the eyes of detectives. Therefore, since its inception, it has never been exposed. Every morning, Gu orders her partner, a Yong woman named Mao Aibao, to deliver two bags of red pills to the Bund outside Second Malu, each bag worth six yuan and forty cents. Mao receives four cents for transportation, and the rest is handed over to Gu. Recently, at 6:45 AM, Mao was delivering red pills to the Bund outside Second Malu when she was stopped by Hongkou Police Detective Wu Deyu, Detective Bao Ni Jialai, and Chinese Constable No. 325 while passing Broadway Road and Wuchang Road. Suspecting her, they searched her and found two bags of red pills, which they took back to the police station. After Mao confessed, they went to No. 21, Lane 122, Yuanfang Road, and arrested Gu, finding four bags of red pills under the sofa. She was sent to the First Special Court and prosecuted under Article 263 of the Criminal Code. Yesterday morning, Judge Ye Shengchao opened the Fifth Criminal Court for interrogation. Police Lawyer Jiang Baolian explained the case and, after examining the case, stated that it was in fact in line with Article 257, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Code and requested that the charging articles be corrected. Then, the detectives testified about the search, and when Gu Jindi was questioned, she denied it outright, claiming she had been framed, and hired a lawyer to defend her, saying that Gu Jindi's husband had also been falsely imprisoned and then released and that the detectives who handled the case were reprimanded by the chief patrol officer, resulting in a grudge against him, and thus the occurrence of this case. After Judge Ye verified the confession, he announced the judgment in court: Gu Jindi was sentenced to two years in prison for continuously selling morphine compounds, and Mao Aibao was sentenced to one year and six months in prison for aiding in the sale of morphine compounds. The six bags of red pills were confiscated.

Bales Company Sues Comprador for Embezzlement 159

Defendant Claims Accounting Dispute; Court Orders Rescheduling for Further Inquiry

Yin Fugen, a Ningbo native and comprador for the British company Bales Limited, embezzled the company's funds and fled back to his hometown. After the employer reported it to the police, Yin returned to Shanghai and surrendered himself. He was sent to the First Special District Court for investigation and interrogation, as previously reported. The police investigation found that Yin had fraudulently obtained 7,989 yuan from Bales from July 15th to November 15th. In addition, because he also continued to embezzle funds from the British company White Law Company, he is now being prosecuted under Article 339 of the Criminal Code in a consolidated case. Yesterday morning, Judge Jiang of the First Special Court interrogated him. Police Lawyer Zhang Shizhu stated the defendant's embezzlement process, saying that he signed a contract with Bales in the 21st year of the Republic to serve as a comprador, stipulating that his commission for transactions was 1%. In June of this year, the contract was revised and the commission was also changed to 3%. The defendant's method of defrauding money was to forge household names such as Chaoji, Fuji, and Xingji, etc. When questioned, the shareholders stated that after the contract was revised, the commission he received was still 1%, so the matter was purely an accounting dispute. The court then ordered rescheduling for further inquiry.

Chen Bohe Illegally Opens Hospital to Collect Money Without Registration 160

Using the Pretext of Guaranteed Treatment for Lung Disease, Xu Wenfeng is Deceived

Chen Bohe, a native of Taizhou, Jiangbei, 29 years old, used to be an assistant officer in the military medical office of the newly compiled 10th Division of the Army, so he gained some experience in medicine. After being discharged, he returned to Shanghai and masqueraded as a doctor, practicing medicine. He first opened the Dehe Hospital on North Shanxi Road, and then moved to Changping Road, renaming it Changping Hospital. Chen served as the president and doctor of the hospital, but because Chen's medical skills were not good, business was poor and the place was deserted. After opening for several months, he accumulated a huge amount of rent. Chen was unable to maintain it and had no choice but to flee. The landlord filed a lawsuit in the Civil Court of the First Special Court. After several hearings, Dong was found absent and a default judgment was made, ordering Chen Bohe to repay 200 yuan plus statutory interest. However, Chen was not afraid of the law and secretly continued to defraud money as a slick doctor. On one hand, he opened the Nanyang Hospital at No. 1209 Roberts Road, indiscriminately issuing flyers and arbitrarily exaggerating, saying that he could cure all diseases and would not refuse poor patients. Xu Wenfeng, a native of Suqian who lived on Roberts Road, was deceived by the flyer. His five-year-old son Xu Wentong was suffering from a severe illness, so in October he took his son to Nanyang Hospital for treatment. Initially, he paid a consultation fee of two corners once or twice. Later, Chen Bohe suddenly told Xu Wenfeng that his son was suffering from tuberculosis and could not be cured in a short time. He suggested that Chen provide guaranteed treatment in order to be effective. Xu agreed and discussed the price of guaranteed treatment. Chen initially asked for one hundred yuan, then settled on sixty yuan, stating that half of the amount, thirty yuan, must be paid first, and the remainder paid later. Xu paid thirty yuan, and Chen issued a receipt and a guaranteed treatment voucher. After several treatments, not only did the illness not improve, but he was also charged ten yuan. Recently, Xu refused to pay the remaining twenty yuan because his son's illness had not improved. Chen also refused to treat the illness as an excuse. Xu then became suspicious and discussed it with Wu Xingen, the president of the Fourth District Branch of the Shanghai Citizens' United Association. Wu sent a letter to the Social Affairs Bureau and the Health Department of the Public Works Department to investigate. According to the reply, Chen Bohe was not registered and was not a doctor. Xu then realized he had been deceived and reported the situation to the Putuo Road Police Station, which dispatched detectives to arrest Chen Bohe, seizing the seals of Dehe Hospital, Changping Hospital, and Chen Bohe, and taking them to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special Court. Police Lawyer Zhang Tianyin, in addition to prosecuting under Article 340 of the Criminal Code, also stated the case, followed by Xu Wenfeng's complaint about the defendant's treatment of his son's illness and the payment of consultation fees. The defendant's testimony was evasive. Judge Liu Yugui verified the confession and ordered Chen to be returned to custody, with a rescheduled hearing in seven days. He also ordered the police to send the medicine to the Health Department of the Public Works Department for testing.

French Concession Bailu Road; A Morphine Manufacturing Operation is Cracked; The Main Culprit Has Fled, The Woman Who Recently Gave Birth Granted Bail; The Police Request an Extension to Arrest the Main Culprit 161

French Police Superintendent Piquesky (transliteration) and Chinese Detective Gao Hongxuan learned on the morning of the 8th that someone was secretly manufacturing morphine in a private operation inside No. 8 Baoanfang, Bailu Road, Nanyang Bridge, and selling it in the city, violating the government's strict prohibition of drugs. Therefore, at noon that day, they led detectives He Zongyu, Chen Tinghuai, Zheng Jikun, Wang Wenwei, Li Hezhang, etc., to secretly search the address. Upon arriving at the number and knocking on the door, the main culprit, a Cantonese man surnamed Lin, had already heard the sound and jumped over the sun deck to escape. Only the suspected Cantonese Wu Chenghe (49 years old) and Wu Zhangshi (37 years old, who had just given birth and was resting in bed) and two other men and women were apprehended. Inside the second floor and the mezzanine, they seized a motor manufacturing machine, two green jars, a wind furnace, a lead bucket sieve, and large glass bottles for storing strong acid, etc., several pounds of manufactured morphine, and raw material drugs, etc. (The packaging paper boxes of each raw material were mostly labeled with the signs of a certain pharmacy), and took them to the police station together. According to Wu and others, the second landlord, Zheng Guozhang from Chaozhou, lives at No. 83 Dongxinqiao Street. The detectives went to the address to arrest him, but Zheng had already fled after hearing the news. Only his wife Zheng Wushi (33 years old, Chaozhou native) was arrested. Yesterday afternoon, they were sent to the First Criminal Court of the Second Special Court. Police Lawyer Yuan Jiadan stated the case and requested an extension to further detain the fugitive main culprit and thoroughly investigate the case before filing a lawsuit for interrogation. When Wu Chenghe was questioned, he said, "I am a co-tenant. The second floor was rented by a man surnamed Lin, who moved in on the evening of November 21st and said he was doing a liquid medicine business. I didn't know he was manufacturing morphine." Wu Zhangshi said, "I didn't know Lin was making morphine. I gave birth last month on the 22nd and haven't completed my confinement. My child died six days after birth. I am resting in bed." Zheng Wushi said, "My husband sells roasted meat. The Baoanfang house was rented on May 1st of this year. I didn't know he was making morphine." Because Wushi was unfamiliar with the Shanghai dialect, her testimony was translated by the defendants. Presiding Judge Wang Gangxu verified the confession and ordered rescheduling for further inquiry on the 14th. Wu Zhangshi was granted bail of 300 yuan to be available for summons at any time. Wu Chenghe and Zheng Wushi were returned to custody. The morphine equipment and raw materials seized were temporarily stored in the stolen goods warehouse.

American Trust Company Bank Begins to Refund Deposits 162

Those with 150 yuan or less will be fully refunded, while those with more will receive 25%; According to the Daily News. The American Trust Company Bank on Xiafei Road in this port, after being affected by the closure of its Harbin headquarters, entrusted lawyer Huang Peizhu to sort out the accounts and raise cash in preparation for refunding depositors' savings. Once all the cash has been raised, it can be fully refunded without any problems. Each depositor has been notified to go and claim it.

Citywide Inspection of Public Places Completed; Those Not Yet in Order Given a Deadline to Correct; Hair Salons Found to be Best in Inspection Results 163

According to the Xin Sheng News Agency, the city's Public Security Bureau conducted an inspection of public places, which lasted for five months. The deadline was repeatedly extended to avoid any omissions or negligence. Now, as a result of the inspection, all places have gradually followed the orders, paying attention to tidiness and cleanliness. Therefore, the New Movement Section of the bureau sent personnel for a final inspection from the 2nd to the 7th of this month, which has now concluded.

Deadline for Correction

After the bureau's final inspection, places that still need to be urgently corrected have been given a specific deadline to correct them. The deadlines are four types: ten days, seven days, five days, and three days. After the deadline has passed, the police from each branch bureau will be responsible for checking and verifying whether the changes have been made, and paying attention to the progress of the items listed in the "Progress Table." If a cross is marked, it means that the improvement has been made. An "x" means that it has not been implemented. If repeated persuasion has been given in the past but no changes have been made, the bureau will impose penalties. After the final inspection deadline, the bureau plans to conduct random spot checks at any time to avoid superficial compliance.

Inspection Results

The results of the bureau's final inspection of public places throughout the city show that the best results in terms of tidiness, cleanliness, and implementation of the New Movement are: first, hair salons; second, restaurants; third, bathhouses; fourth, hotels; and fifth, entertainment venues. The tidiness and cleanliness of hair salons are indeed superior to other public places, so the inspection results are most satisfactory for this type of business.

Provincial Supervisory Office Sends Personnel to Investigate Former Luodian Public Security Bureau Chief Case 165

On April 26th of this year, in Zhao Jia Lane, about two li east of Luodian Town, there were two men wearing blue cloth short shirts and trousers at the home of an old woman surnamed Jin (who usually looked at incense heads, commonly called spirit medium). They falsely claimed to invite the old woman to a certain place to conduct a séance. At that time, the old woman's son, named Jin Zhixiang, returned home from doing business in Shanghai and knew that these two men must be scammers, so he refused their request. Unexpectedly, the two men wearing blue cloth shirts and trousers took out guns and threatened him. Jin suspected they were robbers, so he shouted loudly, and farmers from the surrounding villages arrived and tied one of them up and sent him to the Luodian District Office. Later, Zhou Jintang, the chief of the town's Public Security Branch, heard about it and arrived. Seeing that the two men tied up were plainclothes policemen from the bureau, he immediately retrieved them and apologized to the crowd to end the matter. Unexpectedly, on September 15th, Zhou again accused Jin of using sorcery to treat illnesses, violating police regulations. Therefore, he sent police to arrest Jin and fine him 30 yuan. Unexpectedly, Jin's son Zhixiang refused to accept this and filed a lawsuit with the High Court and also filed a complaint with the Jiangsu Provincial Supervisory Office of the Supervisory Yuan and the Civil Affairs Department. Now it is learned that the Supervisory Office has specially sent personnel to Luodian to investigate in order to understand the truth of the matter. Many witnesses to the case have been summoned.

Deadline for General Registration of Patent Medicines Approaches; New Medicine Association Petitions for Two-Year Extension 167

The National United Association of New Medicine Industries yesterday submitted a petition to the Ministry of Health, stating that the deadline for the general registration of patent medicines should be extended by two years to allow sufficient time for procedures. It is reported that the deadline for the general registration of patent medicines will expire at the end of December of this year. However, considering that there are many types of patent medicines and very few have obtained permits, due to the complicated procedures of revising prescriptions and amending leaflets, it is difficult to complete them in time. There are many more who have not yet submitted their registration. The period from now until the deadline for general registration is very pressing, and it is certainly impossible for industries in various places to complete the registration procedures in time. Therefore, it has been resolved by the first session of the association's representative assembly to submit a petition to the Ministry of Health, requesting that the deadline for general registration be extended by two years. On the one hand, the association will do its utmost to urge industries in various places to handle the registration of patent medicine products in accordance with laws and regulations during the extension period in order to live up to the Ministry's intention to protect the new medicine industry. Please grant approval to facilitate handling and allow sufficient time for procedures.

General Overview of the Shanghai Soap Industry 172

(Fifth of the General Overview of Shanghai Industry and Commerce) Edited by China Credit Information Service

1. Development of the Shanghai Soap Manufacturing Industry

Alkaline substances can remove dirt and grime. Our ancestors and rural women in remote areas today often use rice straw ashes or soapberry pods to wash things because they contain alkaline properties. After the opening of trade ports, Chinese people began to use foreign soap. Foreign soap is manufactured using scientific methods, and in addition to containing better alkaline substances, it also contains some animal or vegetable oils, so it has greater cleaning power and does not damage clothing as easily as grass ash or soapberry pods. As a result, foreign soap entered our country unimpeded.

The first foreign soap imported into our country was "Lihe" soap. In recent years, the "Xiangmao" and "Beiji" brands of foreign goods have also been selling well in the market. During this time, British and Japanese capital successively came to Shanghai to set up factories for manufacturing, directly selling their products to Shanghai and inland areas, monopolizing the soap market in our country. The "Shanghai Oil and Fat Co., Ltd." (Japanese-owned), established two years before the founding of the Republic of China (1910), and the "China Soap Co., Ltd." (British-owned), established one year before the founding of the Republic of China, were the two major forces that rose at that time. To this day, they are still the dominant players in the Shanghai soap industry.

Although soap manufacturing is a type of chemical industry, it does not involve the production of chemical raw materials but merely the reconfiguration of already-made chemical semi-finished products. The technology is not complicated, and the required capital can be large or small. Therefore, soon after the import of foreign soap, when British and Japanese capital were establishing a foundation in China, Chinese merchants who rose up to imitate them were also quite numerous. For example, Chinese merchant Dong Fuqing established the "Yumao Soap Factory" in Zhabei, Shanghai, which was the pioneer of soap factories in our country. Those that followed included "Yimao" in the first year of the Republic, and "Nanyang," "Lida," and "Dingfeng" in the second year of the Republic. The newly established Chinese soap factories in Shanghai are listed by year as follows:

Year Number of Factories

Years 1-5 of the Republic 6

Years 11-15 of the Republic 7

Years 21-24 of the Republic 3

First half of the year

Year Number of Factories

Years 6-10 of the Republic 3

Years 16-20 of the Republic 4

The above table is calculated based on existing factories that have joined the trade association. Factories that have closed down or have not joined the association are not included. Therefore, the actual number of factories should be slightly more than what is listed in the above table. Even if we only consider the existing factories that have not joined the association, there are about ten. Overall, there are quite a few Chinese soap factories in Shanghai, but because of their small capital and mostly manual manufacturing techniques, it is still very difficult to compete with foreign companies. In recent years, the Shanghai soap industry has also been in a recession. During the January 28th Incident, a total of six factories were directly destroyed or indirectly affected and closed down. Although the devastation of the military conflict has passed, the misfortune of economic panic has not been eliminated. Contraction is often heard of. How to unite and strive for survival to overcome the current difficulties is what the soap industry should work together to achieve.

2. General Overview of Various Soap Factories in Shanghai (Chinese and Foreign)

According to a recent survey by our institute, there are currently more than 30 Shanghai Chinese soap manufacturing factories. Among them, 24 have joined the trade association (the trade association was established in the winter of the 17th year of the Republic). The factory names, capital, and production volume are listed on the left for reference:

Factory Name Establishment Capital Annual Output (Units: Cases) Trademark

Guangtong Soap Company Year 19 of the Republic 40,000 yuan —— Linked Rings

Invincible Perfume Soap Factory Year 24 of the Republic 50,000 yuan —— Butterfly

According to the above table, the largest Chinese factory in terms of capital is Wuzhou Guben Soap Medicine Factory, with 300,000 yuan. The next largest are Nanyang, Wudi, Guangtong, and Central, with between 40,000 and 60,000 yuan. The rest are small factories with 10,000 yuan or several thousand yuan. However, even for Wuzhou, compared to the foreign factories in Shanghai, the capital of just the British-owned China Soap Company (8 million yuan) exceeds the total capital of the 25 Chinese factories listed above. No wonder the national industry cannot stand alone and compete with foreign companies. There are not many foreign factories in Shanghai, but their capital is very strong. The main ones are as follows:

1. China Soap Co., Ltd. The establishment date and capital have been mentioned earlier. The factory is located at 2310 Yangshupu Road, covering an area of over 100 mu. Its head office is located on the second floor of the Mackenzie Building on the Bund. Branch offices are established in major ports such as Tianjin, Nanchang, Xiamen, and Shenyang. The company was formed by the merger of Lever Brothers, Wesson, Price's, and 厚丰 four soap companies. It is extremely large in scale. Its products are divided into household soap and cosmetic soap (mainly the former). There are many brands, such as Lux soap, Lever antiseptic soap, Xiangmao, Beiji, Sunlight, etc. The daily output of household soap alone reaches six to seven thousand cases, and the average annual turnover can reach 10 million yuan.

2. Shanghai Oil and Fat Co., Ltd. The factory was established one year earlier than the China Soap Factory. It was built on Bimin Road, and the sales office was located on Henan Road (the Linbao foreign firm is also its sales agency). The registered capital is 500,000 yuan, and the paid-up capital is 250,000 yuan. It has 35 machines and employs about 120 workers. The annual output is 1 million dozen of perfume soap and 900,000 jin of oil and fat.

3. The First Company (also known as the First Industrial Pharmaceutical Co., Ltd.) is a branch from the Japanese head office. It was established in the 7th year of the Republic. The factory is located at 55 Hejian Road, covering an area of about 4 mu. Since last year, the capital has been expanded to 1 million Japanese yen, with a paid-up capital of 625,000 yuan and accumulated reserves of about 20 Japanese yen. The factory mainly manufactures and sells industrial soap. The annual output is 8,640 cases of soap, and the annual turnover reaches 200,000 Japanese yen. The sales office is located at 355 Miller Road.

4. Raw Materials for Manufacturing Soap

The main raw materials for manufacturing soap are alkali and oil. Perfume soap also requires various fragrances, but they account for a very small proportion. There are many types of alkali, which can be mainly divided into three types: soda ash, caustic soda, and sodium metasilicate. Very little is produced domestically, and most is imported. The import volume of soda ash and caustic soda in the last four years is statistically shown as follows (unit: Customs Gold Unit):

Year 21 Year 22 Year 23 January-October Year 24

Soda Ash 1,691,581 1,135,867 1,115,024 872,036

Caustic Soda 1,026,733 1,045,476 1,043,236 1,096,139

Year 21 National Shanghai

Household and Laundry Soap 147 44

Cosmetic Soap 578 282

Note: Unit: 1,000 Customs Gold Units.

The import amounts of both are trending downward. The main reason should be the decline in the domestic market and the decrease in people's purchasing power. However, household soap decreased by two-thirds in three years, while cosmetic soap decreased by only one-fifth. This indicates the increasing development of Chinese factories that manufacture household soap. In addition, the result of the competition between Wuzhou Guben Soap and Xiangmao Soap of the British-owned China Soap Company is also quite consistent with this theory. According to statistics, Wuzhou Guben Soap Factory was indeed established in the 10th year of the Republic, but its development has only been in recent years. In the 18th year of the Republic, the annual turnover was only over 2 million yuan, and the annual profit increased from 20,000 yuan to 300,000 yuan in the 23rd year of the Republic. The main key is that the sales of Xiangmao in Shanghai have been taken over by Guben. Although Xiangmao repeatedly lowered prices for dumping, it still failed to reverse the trend. Therefore, everything depends on our efforts. According to the first and ninth issues of the Federation of Labor Unions, the crude soap produced by Chinese factories in Shanghai has less moisture and more pure soap content than those produced by foreign companies. This kind of substantial improvement is the foundation for the success of the national soap industry in our country. The chemical test results are extracted below to inform the people of the country:

However, at present, the capital of each Chinese factory is limited, and the output is not high. In addition to selling in Shanghai, the soap produced cannot be widely sold in other ports in the interior. Therefore, foreign factories still control the power of frost in North China, South China, and the upper reaches of the Yangtze River. It is hoped that all factories will work together to improve products, expand production, so that the people of the whole country can use soap made by Chinese people, which will make a great contribution to the revival of the national economy.

Education News

The Executive Yuan Approves the Ministry of Education's Administrative Plan for This Year 173

The Ministry of Education's administrative plan for the entire year of 1935 (from July of this year to June of 1936) was previously prepared by the Ministry and submitted to the Executive Yuan for review. It has now been approved. The original text of the administrative plan is as follows:

(A) Matters Concerning Higher Education (1) Revise the regulations for universities and colleges; (2) Designate national universities to prepare special mechanical engineering classes; (3) Consolidate higher education funding in various provinces; (4) Sequentially formulate curriculum and equipment standards for various colleges and various specialized schools of universities; (5) Investigate the achievements and status of research work in various universities; (6) Formulate scholarship methods for schools above the specialized school level in various provinces and cities; (7) Formulate methods for universities to set up scholarships and bursaries; (8) Based on the inspection reports of 1934, urge public and private universities, independent colleges, and specialized schools to make practical improvements; (9) Examine the management of various private universities, independent colleges, and specialized schools that received subsidies this year; (10) Continue to ban private schools above the specialized school level with poor performance; (11) Strictly review the admission qualifications, enrollment quotas, staff employment, and financial status of new students in public and private schools above the specialized school level this year; (12) Organize and compile the cards of graduates over the years; (13) Hold screening exams for graduates and students of unapproved and closed private schools above the specialized school level; (14) Correct the establishment of departments and groups in various specialized schools to meet local needs; (15) Plan to set up special commissioners for managing students studying in Europe and the United States (temporarily request embassies to designate commissioners to be responsible for handling); (16) Review and announce the list of foreign universities and specialized schools to be formally recognized; (17) Compile and print the National Higher Education Statistics for 1933-1934; (18) Investigate the general situation of national higher education in 1935.

(B) Matters Concerning Middle Schools and Normal Schools (1) Urge various provinces and cities to complete the standards for the establishment and funding allocation of secondary schools as soon as possible; (2) Revise the table of weekly teaching hours for each subject in each semester of senior and junior high schools; (3) Determine the detailed teaching items for each subject in senior and junior high schools; (4) Promulgate the general outline of management methods for secondary schools; (5) Compile and print the Secondary Education Statistics for 1933-1934; (6) Compile and print the General Situation of the Graduation Joint Examinations for Students of Middle Schools and Normal Schools held by various provinces and cities in 1934; (7) Continue to compile the test standards for each subject in middle schools; (8) Enforce the inspection of teachers in middle schools and normal schools in various places; (9) Improve the methods of cultivating teachers for secondary schools; (10) Reward outstanding middle schools and normal schools, and ban poor-performing middle schools and normal schools.

(C) Matters Concerning Vocational Education (1) Investigate the general situation of national vocational education in 1935; (2) Compile and print the General Situation of National Vocational Education in 1934; (3) Continue to inspect vocational education in various provinces and cities and compile and print the second volume of inspection reports; (4) Compile the fifth volume of course schedules, teaching material outlines, and equipment summaries for various types of vocational schools; (5) Translate the second and third volumes of vocational guidance reference materials; (6) Investigate the general situation of public nursing and midwifery vocational schools and set a deadline for handling the registration of private nursing and midwifery vocational schools; (7) Hold vocational guidance workshops; (8) Hold summer training courses for agricultural teachers in agricultural vocational schools; (9) Designate well-managed nursing and midwifery vocational schools to prepare for the training of nursing and midwifery teachers; (10) Formulate methods for training teachers in middle schools, normal schools, labor courses, and vocational schools.

(D) Matters Concerning Elementary Education (1) Revise the curriculum standards for kindergartens and elementary schools; (2) Determine the teaching points for each subject in elementary schools; (3) Compile and print the Elementary Education Statistics for 1933-1934; (4) Investigate the general situation of national elementary education and compulsory education in 1935; (5) Urge elementary education research associations in various provinces, counties, and cities across the country to actively conduct research; (6) Investigate excellent elementary schools across the country and compile and print the general situation of excellent elementary schools across the country; (7) Compile and print the research reports on the first and second batches of questions issued by the Ministry to the national elementary school teaching research association; (8) In accordance with the provisions of the general outline of the interim measures for the implementation of compulsory education and its detailed rules for implementation, actively promote compulsory education from this year; (9) Formulate various regulations concerning compulsory education; (10) Formulate short-term elementary school curriculum standards; (11) Modify and compile various textbooks and teaching materials for short-term elementary schools; (12) Inspect compulsory education and elementary education across the country, reward personnel of educational administrative agencies with excellent performance, and punish personnel of educational administrative agencies with poor performance.

(E) Matters Concerning Social Education (1) Announce the first batch of simplified character lists and implementation methods; (2) Cast bronze molds of phonetic Chinese characters and promote methods to promote phonetic Chinese characters; (3) Plan to urge educational administrative agencies in various provinces and cities to actively promote mass schools; (4) Supervise and guide various libraries to improve the editing of textbooks and books for mass schools; (5) Investigate and organize mass readings; (6) Supervise various provinces and cities to promote labor education; (7) Review the social education budget for each province and city across the country this year and prepare and announce the table; (8) Compile and print the national social education statistics for 1932-1934; (9) Investigate the general situation of national social education in 1935; (10) Print and distribute the National Calendar and Mongolian and Tibetan National Calendar for 1936; (11) Formulate regulations for the appointment and treatment of social education personnel; (12) Announce various methods for promoting educational broadcasting; (13) Hold training classes for radio guidance personnel; (14) Appoint lecturers for this year's extermination and nurturing broadcasting; (15) Examine the educational halls and bureaus in various provinces and cities to urge secondary schools and civil education centers to install radios and utilize educational broadcasting; (16) Continue to send personnel to check the antiquities of the Palace Museum; (17) Continue to plan the construction of the Central Library and Museum; (18) Plan to implement various methods of film education.

(F) Matters Concerning Mongolian and Tibetan Education (1) Formulate implementation measures for promoting education in border areas; (2) Follow the central government's decision to subsidize the educational funding of border provinces and properly allocate the subsidy; (3) Inspect the education of Mongolian, Tibetan, and Miao people in border provinces; (4) Supervise educational administrative agencies in border provinces to establish normal schools and elementary schools of all levels and short-term elementary schools for Mongolian, Tibetan, and Hui, and Miao people on schedule; (5) Complete the translation of short-term elementary school textbooks in both Chinese and Mongolian; (6) Start compiling Chinese-Tibetan and Chinese-Hui double-language textbooks for national language and short-term elementary schools; (7) Continue to investigate the general situation of Mongolian, Tibetan, Hui, and Miao education in border provinces.

Ministry of Education Explanation of Compendium of Educational Laws and Regulations 174

The Ministry of Education recently issued two official documents regarding the interpretation of educational laws and regulations, which are compiled below:

(1) The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education submitted a request for interpretation of various ambiguities in the revised regulations for private schools concerning the board of directors. The Ministry issued an instruction to the department, stating that the submitted request for interpretation of various ambiguities in the revised regulations for private schools concerning the board of directors has been reviewed item by item as follows: (1) When the number of founders is excessive, one to three persons may be mutually elected as ex officio members of the board of directors; the remaining founders are not within the board of directors. (2) If an ex officio member resigns for some reason, the method of re-election should be handled in accordance with the articles of association of the board of directors. (3) The organization and powers of the board of directors, as well as the term of office and re-election methods of the directors, shall be stipulated in the articles of association of the board of directors in accordance with Article 13 of the revised regulations for private schools, and shall be submitted to the competent educational administrative authority for approval when the board of directors applies for registration. (4) If an ex officio member of the board of directors has illegal conduct, it shall be reported to the competent educational administrative authority for approval. (5) Once the board of directors has been organized and established, the number of directors and the method of re-election shall be handled in accordance with the articles of association of the board of directors. Founders who are not directors shall not interfere, etc. (2) The Qingdao Municipal Bureau of Education requested an interpretation regarding various ambiguities in the examination of teachers in middle schools and normal schools. The Ministry of Education approved the following instructions: (1) Graduates of university undergraduate or specialized courses and specialized schools, the subjects for which they request examination should, in principle, be those they have specialized in. However, those who have also studied other subjects and whose performance is indeed excellent may also be allowed to take the examination. As for subjects for which examination is requested but which were not studied at school, approval cannot be granted. (2) If the original school from which they graduated has now been discontinued and the level of the school is not very clear, the nature and level of the school (admission qualifications, length of study, etc.) should be determined in accordance with the educational laws and regulations at that time. (3) Graduation certificates issued by schools that had not been registered at the time of graduation cannot be considered valid. However, this does not apply to those whose graduation qualifications have been approved retroactively by the competent educational administrative authority in accordance with the Ministry's Announcement No. 8 of the 19th year and Training Order No. 8699 of the 22nd year, and who have completed the re-examination and stamping.

The Problem of Improving Chinese Musical Instruments (1) 183

— Ding Xiexiu

Three or four years ago, Mr. Xiao Youmei, the president of the National Conservatory of Music, raised a question to me during a conversation. He said that flutes in Western musical instruments are very expensive, and it is not easy for students to purchase them. Could the old-fashioned Chinese flute be improved so that it can replace the Western flute, and at the same time, the price can be very low? In other words, can the Chinese flute be turned into a "proletarian" Western flute? I immediately felt a great interest in this question, and at the same time, this question raised two broader questions: (1) Is it necessary and possible to improve Chinese musical instruments? (2) If we believe that Chinese musical instruments should be improved, should the direction of improvement not only pay attention to academic and artistic aspects, but also take into account popularization?

We see very few opinions from Chinese music experts on Chinese musical instruments. From private conversations, there seem to be two extreme views. One is that Chinese musical instruments are too simple and too narrow. Western musical instruments have many types and good quality. Music, of course, has its national character, but musical instruments can be used in common. With Western musical instruments, we can still produce Chinese music. Since others have ready-made and perfect tools, why don't we completely accept them? Furthermore, the evolution of Western music is progressing towards ideal instruments. If Chinese musical instruments are improved, they will only gradually become Western musical instruments. Furthermore, the reason why Chinese musical instruments are Chinese musical instruments may be because of their simplicity. The reason why the erhu is the erhu is because there is too much noise. The reason why the guqin is the guqin is because its sound is just low enough to be inaudible" (this is English writer Russell's description of the Chinese guqin). The other view is that Chinese music was originally very developed. Like all other civilizations, the twelve-tone equal temperament scale structure currently used in the West was invented by the Chinese. Harmony has always existed in Chinese music. Musical instruments were also very developed originally, but they have only been lost now. As long as we are willing to put effort into the waste paper pile, the revival of Chinese music is not difficult to achieve. Furthermore, among the Chinese musical instruments we currently have, there are also many excellent products. The sheng, xiao, dizi, pipa, and guqin each have their own characteristics. If we hold the prejudice of Western musical instruments and make arbitrary changes, for example, increasing the volume of the xiao and guqin, then all the subtle and wonderful points of these two instruments will be lost. We dare not say that the above two extreme views can include all the opinions of Chinese music experts on Chinese musical instruments, but at least they can represent the opinions of two groups of people without any problem. Naturally, the first view mostly belongs to people who study Western music, and the second view mostly belongs to people who study Chinese music.

From the perspective of us laymen, the above two views seem to contain some very obvious truths, but at the same time, they are not without questionable points. Let's first talk about the first view. First, musical instruments are indeed a kind of tool, but at the same time, each has its own individual timbre, just as food is a material for nourishing life, but different people have different tastes, and writing is a tool for expressing thoughts, but different writing has different forms and structures. Although in terms of writing, some people advocate abolishing Chinese characters and using Roman letters, and some people even advocate abolishing all existing writing and using Esperanto, in terms of food, it seems that some people believe that cooking should be abolished and chemical pills should be used instead, but this is entirely from a utilitarian point of view. Whether it can be done, whether it should be done, of course, are all still problems. If we think from the aspect of enjoyment, it seems that people who appreciate literature and art, it is best to be proficient in all kinds of writing, and people who love delicious food, it is best to have both Western and Chinese food, and Longjing coffee, which is more suitable. However, this is still an equal treatment of all kinds of things. In fact, a nation naturally has a special feeling for its inherent writing, taste, and music. People who have lived abroad for many years have probably had an experience similar to the following. People who have lived abroad for many years, whenever they open a hometown association or alumni association to play music programs, are mostly respectfully listening to foreign music. As soon as they hear Chinese tunes, they will involuntarily be beaming with joy. Of course, there are factors of not knowing foreign music and homesickness, but it cannot be said that it is not a natural response of Chinese people to their own national tunes.

Children's Educational Novel

Little Men (120) 184

— Original by Louisa M. Alcott, translated by Zheng Xiaocang

But the moon's round face had not yet peered over the mountain top to break her hope, and she had already fallen asleep, leaning against the small thatched pavilion formed by tall ferns, deeply immersed in a sweet dream, in which she saw many fireflies, blue skirts, pits and valleys of berries, and Robb was wiping away the tears of a black cow, which was crying and complaining, "I want to go home! I want to go home!"

〇〇〇〇〇〇〇〇〇〇〇〇

The children had fallen asleep, and the buzzing of the nearby mosquitoes helped them to fall into a deep sleep, but their family at home was very alarmed. The hay wagon arrived at five o'clock, and the rest of the people had arrived at the fence on time to wait, but Jack, Amy, Nan, and Rob were not seen. This time, it was not Rice, but Frank who was driving the wagon. When the children told him that others had returned home from the forest, he looked displeased and said, "They have to leave Robb and let him take the wagon back. He will be very tired from walking a long way."

"That road is shorter, and they will be carrying him," said Tafie, who was eager to eat his dinner.

"Are you sure that Nan and Robb went with them?"

"Of course; I saw them climb over that pile of walls, singing that it was already five o'clock, and Jack was shouting that they were going home on another road," Tommo explained again.

"Then that's best, let's all go together," so the firewood wagon, carrying the tired children and many full buckets, rattled back.

The first annual Shanghai Open Individual Table Tennis Championship for the Junior Cup, organized by the Junior Division of the Shanghai YMCA at Eight Immortals Bridge, has been underway since the first of this month. It is said that the association is selling admission tickets to raise funds for the city's underprivileged children's recreational event. The tickets are priced at 20 cents each. Grains: Rumors of U.S. Abandoning Silver Policy Again; Flour and Wheat Plummet 201

The flour market was stable at first, but then it plummeted again. Quotations for foreign wheat from Chicago and Canada fell by about 0.2 jiao. However, at the opening, sentiment was relatively strong due to the sharp rebound the previous day, and near-term contracts were stable, while far-term contracts were slightly better. But after the second round of trading, rumors that the U.S. would abandon its silver policy caused the bulls to become nervous and sell off, causing the market to fall uniformly, dropping by as much as 0.3 to 0.4 fen compared to the opening. When the afternoon session opened, it was calm at first, but in the second round of trading, another large amount of bull liquidation caused a further drop of 0.1 to 0.2 fen. After the third round, sentiment gradually stabilized, and there were fewer sellers. Near-term contracts remained unchanged, while far-term contracts rose by 0.1 fen. Observing the later trend, if spot foreign wheat is active in the market, sentiment will likely continue to soften.

Metals: White Lead Sheets Rise and Fall 206

White lead sheets #5 and #6 have been heavily sought after by battery factories recently, and market supplies have been almost completely purchased. Prices have soared, with offers reaching as high as 35 yuan per piece, but there is still no stock available for purchase. In addition, the market situation for other colors such as #1 and #9 is not very bleak because small-batch transactions are still common. The price for #2 is 29 yuan, and for #9 it is 26 yuan. However, there has been no trading in other colors such as #3, #4, #7, #8, #10, and #12 recently. The stagnation of the market is truly beyond what industry insiders could have predicted. As a result, prices are also extremely weak. #3 is quoted at 28.5 yuan, #4 at 28 yuan, #7 and #8 at 25.5 yuan, and #10 and #12 are quoted at around 27 yuan. It is heard that the overseas price has recently been 19 pounds, 17 shillings, and 6 pence, which seems to be an improvement of 17 shillings and 6 pence compared to before.

Essays

The Taste of Winter 210

—(Hua Ling)

— Winter Arrives in the Human World —

In the faint sunlight, with a slight, sometimes raging, roar of the northwest wind, the wheel of the seasons has rolled into the last season of the year.

"Winter", in the eyes of the rich, may not be as charming as spring, nor as bright and refreshing as autumn, but the only suffering is the cold air. However, with cars that come and go without being assaulted by the cold, and warm electric stoves and radiators in their homes, even if snowflakes are flying outside, they can say "Ha ha, there is no winter this year." If they are happy, they can enjoy the snow with a cup of wine, and perhaps even praise winter, taking a quote out of context, "Winter is lovely, it does not deceive me."

Look, the rich say "There is no winter this year", but the poor are shivering in the northwest wind, their teeth chattering. However, I tell you, those who are shivering in the northwest wind seem to deserve our sympathy, but I think they also each get what they deserve, because rickshaw pullers, dock workers, and those who sell their labor can sweat in the northwest wind. If they don't sweat, it means they are lazy. Who can sympathize with laziness?

However, with the weather getting cold and the northwest wind blowing, the issue of the rich and the poor is secondary. How will the disaster victims in the disaster areas, without clothing, food, or homes, spend this long winter?

Knitting Yarn 211

—Chen Liang

If one were to say that Chinese women are good at making use of their time, knitting yarn would be the most obvious and widely appreciated example. Female students in classrooms can listen to the teacher's lecture while knitting a yarn turtleneck sweater for their "cousin" with their slender fingers. Even when going to the gatehouse to check for mail, they will be knitting as they walk. They would rather sacrifice half an hour or an hour on applying nail polish than stop knitting yarn for a minute.

On trams, one often sees women wearing glasses, flat-heeled shoes, black armbands, and fountain pens hanging around their necks, huddled in the "first class" corner knitting yarn, their eyes fixed, their minds focused on the two bamboo needles, yet they will not miss their destination. She is a Christian type, a sharp and intelligent woman.

Walking into the park, on the warm sunny lawn, or next to the few maple trees, one will find a gentle and quiet girl busily working with her tender white rubber-like hands, either knitting a yarn hat for her younger brother, a vest for her older brother, or wrist warmers for her mother. The quiet fragrance of flowers, the quiet heart, and the urban poets who sigh repeatedly for the yellow leaves also linger around her, and the title of their poems is "The Girl Knitting Yarn."

The little kid next door also whittled two bamboo chopsticks, and who knows where he got a ball of dirty and unidentifiable yarn, and he knits and unravels it day and night. Recently, he has actually learned to knit patterns, but his father is a poor man who cannot afford a pound or two of yarn, so he has to knit for others, earning a little money to supplement the cost of oil, salt, and firewood. Everyone says that the little kid is smart and has good hands. But what's the use of it? Isn't it just "making clothes for others"? Poor little kid.

When the northwest wind starts blowing and the world is oppressive, the radiator and fur coat class is certainly immune to the cold. Those who have virtuous wives and loving mothers also have yarn sweaters to keep their bodies warm. Lonely people, to whom will they turn? When they see those women knitting yarn. Alas, they should just go ask the little kid!

Pitiful Mother and Child 212

Winter Quilt 213

— Wei Jing

Poets, in winter, find joy in gathering around the stove, composing verses about snow. Philanthropists, in winter, consider the plight of suffering victims, hungry and cold, with compassion. Vulgar men, in winter, seek pleasure in wine and women. I, however, neither compose poetry, nor possess wealth for charity, nor have any interest in such low-class pleasures. Therefore, I have neither fondness nor dislike for winter. I am me, winter is winter, we have nothing to do with each other.

However, in winter, I do have a particular fondness, and that is for being in bed. Although my quilt is not a fully domestic silk and cotton quilt, nor an authentic imported down quilt, being curled up, nice and warm, in an old cotton quilt is quite satisfying. Especially as the time to get out of bed approaches, it becomes even more inviting. At that moment, lingering a little longer, one can truly say that I would not trade it for being king. Because I believe that even the emperor, who has to attend court before dawn, cannot enjoy such leisure.

Whether being in bed is sweet or bitter, it’s really hard to describe, but the feeling is indeed pleasant. When about to get out of bed but not yet, turning over to one side, then to the other, and if there's a hole in the quilt corner, feeling a draft invading, in the blink of an eye, the quilt corner is pulled and tightly wrapped. Ah, at that moment, there's a sense of comfort that loosens every bone. If there are only three to five minutes left before getting out of bed, hugging the quilt tightly, staying warm, and closing one's eyes for a moment of relaxation, that feeling is far superior to a drunkard's cup in hand, by a hundredfold.

Usually, driven by the needs of clothing and food, one has to get up at dawn, and the longing for the quilt always brings a sense of regret. Only when Sunday arrives can one truly indulge. On Sundays in winter, because there are no worries, one usually doesn't wake up until nature calls after the sun is high in the sky. But the weather outside the quilt is like three or four months behind the season inside the quilt. So when the urge to urinate becomes unbearable, one grits one's teeth, crawls out of the quilt to relieve oneself, and then returns to the quilt, truly experiencing the joy of a disaster victim receiving relief. This fondness lasts until midday, when the quilt becomes cold and there's nothing left to be fond of, then one resolutely gets out of bed.

How joyous is the pleasure of being in bed - alas, each winter is only a short three months.

Miscellaneous Thoughts

Random Notes on Fur Goods 214

— Nan Ding

Every winter, when the north wind howls, and the weather is freezing, people often wear fur coats for warmth. Wealthy families wear precious items like fox fur and gray squirrel, while less affluent families have sheepskin. Poor families sometimes even lack cotton clothing, not to mention fur coats.

There are many types of fur goods, of varying prices. Even within the same type of fur, there are differences in quality depending on where it comes from. In winter, people who wear fur coats should have a basic understanding of the sources and quality of fur goods.

Sea Otter: Sea otter is one of the most valuable types of fur. Northerners call it "Hai Hu," while Southerners call it "Hai Long." So "Hai Hu" and "Hai Long" are the same thing. Sea otter comes from the sea. It's an animal that grows in the ocean. Vladivostok produces a lot of it. The fur is thick and black, with a slight reddish-yellow tint, and its warmth is unparalleled. When it's in the sea, there's a thin layer of skin protecting the fur. Removing the skin reveals the warm and thick fur. Because it's difficult to catch, and extremely warm and durable, the price is very high. Moreover, the production is now very low, which naturally makes it even more valuable. Most of the sea otter sold on the market is old stock. Shanghai, especially Daji Cheng, has the most. Last year, they bought a large batch of fur goods from the Palace Museum, including a lot of sea otter, so they held a sea otter sale.

Sable: Sable fur is also a very precious fur, capable of melting ice and snow, so its warmth can be imagined. The largest production area is in Siberia, Russia. Because sables live in cold regions, Siberia has many. The best type is called black gold sable, which is black with golden-red highlights, and has white hairs on the surface, known as silver gun sable. The next best is purple sable, produced in places like Mongolia's Ganmu Que Si. There is also a Qing Gen sable, with green roots, but it is far inferior to purple sable.

Fox Fur: Fox fur is also most abundant in the Mongolian border region. It can be divided into white fox, fire fox, black fox, yellow fox, ordinary fox fur, and sand fox. Black fox is the most expensive, with pure black color and a reddish base. White fox is pure white like snow. Fire fox is the color of fire. Yellow fox is yellow. White fox skin is the most tender and light, feeling like nothing when worn, and its price is slightly lower than black fox. Fire fox is even lower. Yellow fox and ordinary fox fur are lower than fire fox, and sand fox is the cheapest, almost comparable to sheepskin. Fox fur coats are mostly made from fox pelts, which is the fox's body. The rest, made from fox legs, are called fox leg coats. Fox heads and fox paws can also be made into coats, with red fox leg being the most expensive and sand fox being the least.

Gray Squirrel: Gray squirrel has also become a precious item in recent years, with gray back being the best, made from the back skin of gray squirrels. It is produced in Northeast China, outside the customs. The gray squirrel from Jilin Province has thin and tender fur, called Guandong goods, which is the lowest grade of gray squirrel and not durable. Gray squirrels from places like Qiqihar have thick, old skin, with a black color and a reddish tint, called Su Lu squirrel, which is the top choice among gray squirrels. Catching gray squirrels is very strange. They are mostly caught in mountain valleys. After a heavy fog in winter, you can enter the mountains to catch them, and they are everywhere, and you can get a lot. If there is no heavy fog, it is impossible to find a gray squirrel. Therefore, people who catch gray squirrels consider foggy days to be the opportunity to enter the mountains, and it must be in winter, because the fur is full in winter. In autumn and summer, it is not yet fully grown, and in spring, it is the shedding season, so it is not usable.

Other fur goods include Tan skin from Gansu, Qing Zong sheep from Mongolia, and other types of fur, each with different origins. Shanghai's fur goods are the best in the country, because people who collect fur goods first select them through Shanghai merchants and then send them to other places. Therefore, Shanghai is the most suitable place to buy high-quality fur goods.

Little Western Paradise 215

— By Zhang Henshui

Chapter 22: Knightly Words Move Painted Lips, Beautiful Women Gather to Discuss, False Affection Startles Jade Wrists, Suffering Girl Escapes Captivity

Zhiqian had no choice but to stand up and wave his hand at him repeatedly. At the same time, he kept looking at the window on the back wall and pouting. When Bei Hai looked over there, it was Yueying's grandmother and mother, tidying themselves up and walking towards the back door. Behind them, there was also a man, who was the attendant of the Blue Commissioner. He followed behind them, grumbling. Bei Hai said: Mr. Cheng, does this situation mean that another problem has arisen? Zhiqian smiled: Of course there is some kind of relationship, otherwise, the attendant wouldn't bother following them like that. Bei Hai's eyes were fixed on the window, not moving at all. Only when he couldn't see the shadows of these three people did he say to Zhiqian: The Blue Commissioner came here to find something to do. People like Jia Duocai, who trample on women's rights, are worth investigating. Zhiqian smiled: Speaking from your standpoint, you probably think that everyone agrees with you. This was a casual remark, but it made it impossible for Bei Hai to continue the conversation. He calmed himself down after hearing these words, sat for a while, and then said, Mr. Cheng, do you have something to do? Zhiqian thought to himself, you suddenly came to find me today, and you suddenly want to leave, you know whether there is anything to do, why are you asking me? He smiled and said: I don't have anything to do, but I advise you to be more indifferent to things, don't be too enthusiastic. The more enthusiastic people are, the bigger the nails they hit. Bei Hai said: I'm not very enthusiastic, but I like to speak fairly. What does this matter have to do with me? I'm just meddling. As he said this, he had already started walking towards the outside. This time he didn't leave through the front door, but went straight to the back door. Sure enough, the Blue Commissioner's attendant was leaning against the doorframe, looking into the small doorway across the street. The two women were still walking in the courtyard. Bei Hai stood at the door and looked into the doorway. When the attendant saw him like this, he looked him up and down. Bei Hai was a little embarrassed, thinking that if he walked away, it would probably make people even more suspicious. So he smiled at the attendant and said: Mr. Commissioner thinks, aren't these two women very pitiful? The attendant had never heard anyone call him Mr., and seeing a student-like person addressing him like this, he was very happy. (375)

Winter Song 216

— Juan

A gust of north wind assaults, I know winter has arrived in the world. Winter! Don't be too cruel! In a blink of an eye, the Spring God will arrive, and finally drive you away. I have already compiled this winter special page, filled with an atmosphere of solemnity and desolation; I want to find some beautifying poems and lyrics to embellish it, but I scratched my head and pondered for a long time, but couldn't find anything. Oh, I have it, the day before yesterday, my brother Zhang Jinglu of Shanghai Magazine Company sent me several rare Chinese literary series, and my brother Ping Jinya of Central Bookstore also sent me several rare Chinese academic series. There is a Yuan Dynasty drama in the series, and a Neon Clothes Continued Score in the library. There are some pretty good tunes in it. When I turned them over, I found a Winter Song, and I quickly copied it below.

When winter comes, the wind gets worse and it clears up suddenly. I pick sparse plums and soak old vases, enjoying the remaining happiness. At that time, I follow my heart, and the mountains are charming, he is angry and hateful, good is suitable and evil is also suitable. Until the morning I look at him without turning my eyes, carefully watching him, forgetting the cold and heat, forgetting hunger and satiety, forgetting the cold. (See Yuan Dynasty Zaju)

Chrysanthemum branches are old, bamboo leaves are dry, it is only the beginning of the cold weather. The person has left, the hundreds of diseases of Qingqiu, dragging and teasing me, my mind is tired and my love is foolish. All day long, I am always sentimental, sitting alone in an empty room, lonely and deserted, searching and searching. The beast burner in the golden stove is frequently added, but it can't warm the old red sleeves, the cold penetrates the ice muscle, and the fairy eyebrows are damaged. This sentiment is lingering and subtle, besides plum blossoms, who else can I tell it to? I'm afraid of dusk, I can't bear to see the moon rising in the corner of the building. I only warm the quilt, and even the parrot is afraid of the cold and sleeps late. (Repeated) Waiting for spring to return, waiting for spring to return, but the person does not return, what should I do? (Repeated) (See Neon Clothes Continued Score)

Foreigner Appeals for Refugees 217

— Meng Ruo

A few days ago, this newspaper published a letter from a foreigner, saying that one evening, while passing Difeng Road, he saw two men and two women by the stone wall, each woman holding an infant. The two men were shouting "Selling children." Upon inquiring about their origins, he learned that they were farmers from the north who had fled to Shanghai due to the drought. Now they had exhausted their meager funds and had to sell their children to survive. He immediately offered them financial assistance and appealed to the police, the Royal Hotel, the Salvation Army, a major church, the Chinese and Foreign Relief Association, etc., to take them in, but they were all rejected.

This foreigner is indeed very kind. Seeing several famine refugees trying to sell their children, he was immediately filled with compassion. Not only did he help them with money, but he also appealed to various parties on their behalf. But the result was very disappointing to him. The hotel refused first, and then the charitable organizations closed their doors. So he sighed and said, "Alas! Is there really no place for these hungry birds to perch? Otherwise, why would everyone reject them?"

I think this kind foreigner must be new to China. That's why he was immediately filled with compassion when he saw this human tragedy. In fact, these kinds of things can be found everywhere in our country at any time. Selling children is nothing. Eating children's flesh is not that uncommon either. In this day and age, people say "necessity is the mother of invention." Now the people of our country are so poor that they can't be any poorer!

To be fair, the charitable organizations' refusal to accept these few refugees has its own reasons. Recently, waves of famine refugees from various places have been gathering in Shanghai. If you take in one, you have to take in all. I'm afraid that even if you build a thousand more of the largest shelters, they still won't be able to accommodate everyone.

But are we just going to let them starve and freeze to death? That doesn't make sense either. Foreigners have shown pity for the refugees in our country. Can it be that we are indifferent to our own compatriots and don't think about providing relief? Moreover, Shanghai is the most prosperous place in the country. As long as a group of wealthy people are willing to be generous, accommodating some refugees is not impossible. Therefore, we hope that Shanghai's charitable organizations will expand a few more refugee shelters this year to help our disaster-stricken compatriots. This is our duty, and it is also the morality that humans should have!

Childhood Longings 218

— Lin Hao

Childhood, disappeared as the wrinkles on my forehead marked line by line.

My hometown remains as it was, that little red birch tree that stood on the top of the small hill has grown so tall, swaying its branches in the wind. The mountain is still covered with green grass, dripping with last night's dew in the morning, more lovely in its emerald greenness. The goshawk keeps flapping its wings, flying back and forth in the tall forest, often chanting the song of freedom. But where is my nostalgic and lively childhood?

I have come again to the mysterious little road where I left many traces of childhood. It is a dirt road, a long and endless road covered by long weeds and moss, only exposing a foot-wide center of bare soil. Hide-and-seek, this is a very difficult place to find. People, blindfolded, pounce and grab randomly where the grass moves, but it is rare to be caught.

The grass on the road seems to be longer than it was in my childhood, just like I have grown.

In the clear and calm river, the little fish wag their big tails, still opening their mouths, and if any shadow sweeps across the surface of the river, they will shoot over with a flick of their tails.

If it were still childhood, how I would cherish this natural flow! Unfortunately, my heart is now like a water-scarce desert, unable to squeeze out a drop of refreshing nectar!

In childhood, I remember being afraid when I saw the sea, the surging waves, the turbulent whirlpools, the roaring tides, the magnificent water and sky connected without end, a child's heart beating fast. But in reality? I also felt the greatness of the sea, and that the sea would give you joy in your mind and body.

Now the sea in my heart is so ordinary and monotonous.

My heart is like a withered and dying tree, a desert, numb, as if it has lost its trembling function...

Childhood?

Childhood?
